2:31:1973:0:14:72:420:700:12:Times:12:Times:A:The Roots of Health Inequality and The Value of Intra-Family Expertise
2:32:2043:14:14:72:310:686:12:Times:12:Times:A:Yiqun Chen, Petra Persson, and Maria Polyakova
2:33:2089:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:A:NBER Working Paper No. 25618
2:34:2117:14:14:72:142:658:12:Times:12:Times:A:February 2019
2:35:2130:14:28:72:256:644:12:Times:12:Times:A:JEL No. D12,D83,G22,H1,H4,I13,I14
2:36:2163:28:28:306:339:616:12:Times:12:Times:?:ABSTRACT
2:37:2171:28:14:72:540:588:12:Times:12:Times:A:Mounting evidence documents a stark correlation between income and health, yet the causal mechanisms
2:38:2271:14:14:72:540:574:12:Times:12:Times:A:behind this gradient are poorly understood. This paper examines the impact of access to expertise on
2:39:2371:14:14:72:540:560:12:Times:12:Times:A:health, and whether unequal access to expertise contributes to the health-income gradient. Our empirical
2:40:2475:14:14:72:540:546:12:Times:12:Times:A:setting, Sweden, allows us to shut down inequality in formal access to health care; we first document
2:41:2576:14:14:72:540:532:12:Times:12:Times:A:that strong socioeconomic gradients nonetheless persist. Second, we study the effect of access to health-related
2:42:2688:14:14:72:540:518:12:Times:12:Times:A:expertise – captured by the presence of a health professional in the extended family – on health. Exploiting
2:43:2796:14:14:72:540:504:12:Times:12:Times:A:“admissions lotteries” into medical schools and variation in the timing of degrees, we show that access
2:44:2899:14:14:72:540:490:12:Times:12:Times:A:to intra-family medical expertise has far-reaching health consequences, at all ages: It raises longevity,
2:45:3004:14:14:72:540:476:12:Times:12:Times:A:improves drug adherence and reduces the occurrence of lifestyle-related disease in adulthood, raises
2:46:3104:14:14:72:540:462:12:Times:12:Times:A:vaccination rates in adolescence, and reduces tobacco exposure in utero. Third, we show that the effects
2:47:3208:14:14:72:540:448:12:Times:12:Times:A:of expertise are larger at the lower end of the income distribution – precisely where access to expertise
2:48:3313:14:14:72:540:434:12:Times:12:Times:A:is scarcer. Unequal access to health-related expertise can account for as much as 18% of the health-SES
2:49:3416:14:42:72:439:420:12:Times:12:Times:A:gradient, and may thus play a significant role in sustaining health inequality.
2:50:3495:42:14:72:130:378:12:Times:12:Times:A:Yiqun Chen
2:51:3505:14:14:72:278:364:12:Times:12:Times:A:Department of Health Research and Policy
2:52:3545:14:14:72:167:350:12:Times:12:Times:A:Stanford University
2:53:3564:14:14:72:173:336:12:Times:12:Times:A:150 Governor's Lane
2:54:3583:14:14:72:169:322:12:Times:12:Times:A:Stanford, CA 94305
2:55:3601:14:28:72:183:308:12:Times:12:Times:A:ychen13@stanford.edu
2:56:3621:28:14:72:137:280:12:Times:12:Times:A:Petra Persson
2:57:3634:14:14:72:198:266:12:Times:12:Times:A:Department of Economics
2:58:3657:14:14:72:167:252:12:Times:12:Times:A:Stanford University
2:59:3676:14:14:72:144:238:12:Times:12:Times:A:579 Serra Mall
2:60:3690:14:14:72:169:224:12:Times:12:Times:A:Stanford, CA 94305

3:71:3903:0:28:62:175:719:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:C:1  Introduction
3:72:3918:28:18:62:549:691:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Poorer people have worse health at birth, are sicker in adulthood, and die younger than richer people. Indeed,
3:73:4028:18:17:62:549:673:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:mounting evidence across various disciplines reveals stark correlations between health capital throughout the
3:74:4137:17:18:62:549:656:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:course of life and a range of measures of socioeconomic status (SES), such as education, social class, and income
3:75:4250:18:18:62:492:638:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:(see, e.g., Marmot et al., 1991;Case et al.,2002;Deaton,2002;Currie,2009;Lleras-Muney,2018).
3:76:4342:18:18:77:549:620:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:There is less evidence, however, on the exact pathways between SES and health. Multiple channels have
3:77:4443:18:18:62:549:602:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:been proposed. First, early-life health disparities driven by differentialin uteroconditions or genetic capital may
3:78:4558:18:18:62:549:584:10:g_d0_f2:7:g_d0_f4:B:perpetuate economic inequality (see, e.g.,Currie,2011;Aizer and Currie,2014;Persson and Rossin-Slater,2018).1
3:79:4667:18:18:62:549:566:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Second, differences in health investments through diet, addictive behaviors, physical activity, and utilization of
3:80:4781:18:18:62:549:548:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:healthcare could lead to differential health outcomes.2Third, individuals on the lower rungs of the income ladder
3:81:4894:18:18:62:549:530:10:g_d0_f2:7:g_d0_f4:B:tend to have jobs that involve more manual labor, may experience more stress, and live in more polluted areas.3
3:82:5005:18:18:62:549:512:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Finally, health disparities across the income distribution could be driven by differential treatment conditional
3:83:5117:18:18:62:549:494:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:on disease, due to differences in formal insurance coverage, the quality of available medical care, or individuals’
3:84:5232:18:18:62:549:476:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:ability to navigate the health care system.4The relative contributions of these channels (or existence of others)
3:85:5345:18:18:62:257:458:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:to the health-SES gradient remain unknown.
3:86:5387:18:18:77:549:440:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:In this paper, we investigate one possible underlying factor: the role of (unequal) access to health-related
3:87:5495:18:18:62:549:422:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:expertise. Intuitively, if health-related expertise improves health investment decisions, then an unequal distri-
3:88:5608:18:17:62:549:404:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:bution of expertise across the income ladder would induce a socioeconomic gradient in health. The goal of this
3:89:5718:17:18:62:549:387:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:paper is to shed light on, first, whether better access to expertise improves health; and second, to quantify the
3:90:5831:18:18:62:549:369:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:importance of this channel in sustaining health inequality. We use the presence of a health professional within
3:91:5942:18:18:62:355:351:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the family as a broad measure of access to health-related expertise.
3:92:6010:18:18:77:549:333:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Investigating the causal impact of access to health-related expertise on health and the importance of this
3:93:6116:18:18:62:549:315:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:channel in perpetuating health inequality requires addressing two challenges. First, as emphasized byCurrie
3:94:6223:18:18:62:549:297:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:(2011), analyses of health inequality, while ubiquitous, suffer from a lack of comprehensive data on health
3:95:6330:18:18:62:549:279:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:outcomes, often relying on self-reported health rather than medical records, coupled with a lack of detailed
3:96:6438:18:18:62:550:261:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:measures of socioeconomic status. WhileChetty et al.(2016) overcome this by linking mortality data to tax
3:97:6543:18:15:62:549:243:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:records, an analysis of inequality in health outcomes other than mortality requires data linking individual medical
3:98:6658:15:12:73:549:228:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:1For more evidence on the causal relationship between early-life health and future economic outcomes, see, e.g.,Black et al.(2007);
3:99:6789:12:9:62:549:216:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:Oreopoulos et al.(2008);Bharadwaj et al.(2018a).Almond and Mazumder(2011) document a causal link between low birthweight
3:100:6909:9:10:62:549:207:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:and disability in adulthood. In the context of Sweden,Bharadwaj et al.(2018b) provide causal estimates of own birthweight on a
3:101:7035:10:7:62:225:197:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:range of own outcomes, including mortality.
3:102:7078:7:12:73:549:190:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:2See, e.g.,Rehm et al.(2016) on dietary intake,Hiscock et al.(2012) on smoking, andOgden et al.(2010) on obesity. The
3:103:7195:12:9:62:550:178:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:formation of these health behaviors is poorly understood (Hut and Oster,2018provides the most recent example), and recent
3:104:7316:9:10:62:549:169:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:evidence emphasizes differences in education (e.g.Allcott et al.,2017), peer imitation (e.g.Fowler and Christakis,2008, Rosenquist
3:105:7446:10:9:62:549:159:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:et al.,2010,Rosenquist et al.,2011,Salvy et al.,2012) or costs (e.g.Walker et al.,2010,Allcott et al.,2017and the broader literature
3:106:7578:9:7:62:294:150:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:on food deserts;Meckel,2017on a food program for mothers).
3:107:7636:7:12:73:549:143:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:3See, e.g.,Clougherty et al.(2010) on types of employment,Kunz-Ebrecht et al.(2004) on stress, andIsen et al.(2017) on
3:108:7754:12:10:62:549:131:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:pollution exposure. Also seeFinkelstein et al.(2018a) andBjörkegren(2018) for estimates of the causal effect of location on elderly
3:109:7885:10:9:62:77:121:8:g_d0_f6:6:g_d0_f5:F:mortality and youth health, respectively.4
3:110:7927:9:10:77:549:112:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:Differential access to formal insurance has traditionally been one of the impediments to studying the health-inequality gradient
3:111:8055:10:9:62:549:102:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:in the United States, as insurance coverage varies significantly across income and within income across stages of life. Differences in
3:112:8189:9:9:62:549:93:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:health by income have thus traditionally been partially attributed to differential access to care resulting from differential coverage.
3:113:8324:9:10:62:549:84:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:While Americans at the upper end of the income distribution are likely to be covered by employer-sponsored health insurance from
3:114:8452:10:9:62:549:74:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:birth until they turn 65, coverage is more sporadic in the lower quartiles of the income distribution and may involve moving in and
3:115:8583:9:0:62:249:65:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:out of insurance coverage throughout the lifecycle.
4:116:8635:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:records to detailed measures of income. Second, individuals receive streams of information relevant to their health
4:117:8750:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:from many sources throughout their lifetime, and this exposure is not randomly assigned. Thus, it is difficult to
4:118:8863:18:18:62:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:separate the impact of better access to expertise from other unobservable differences between individuals with
4:119:8973:18:18:62:170:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:and without such access.
4:120:8997:18:17:77:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:We address the first challenge by leveraging Swedish administrative population-wide tax records linked to
4:121:9102:17:18:62:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:inpatient, outpatient, prescription drug, and birth records, described in Section 2. Beyond the availability of
4:122:9213:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:data, Sweden is a particularly attractive empirical context because its universal health insurance system allows
4:123:9325:18:18:62:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:us to shut down another often-hypothesized driver of health inequality: inequality in formal access to health
4:124:9434:18:18:62:549:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:care. In Section 3, we begin by documenting three robust facts in this setting: Health inequality emerges early
4:125:9545:18:18:62:549:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:in life, persists throughout adulthood, and is, at the end of life, as pronounced in Sweden as it is in the United
4:126:9659:18:18:62:549:540:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:States.5These facts underscore the importance of studying other drivers of health inequality, and motivate our
4:127:9769:18:18:62:342:522:10:g_d0_f2:7:g_d0_f4:B:subsequent analysis of the role of (unequal) access to expertise.6
4:128:9835:18:18:77:549:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:To address the second challenge – non-random allocation of access to health-related expertise – we zoom
4:129:9938:18:18:62:549:486:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:into an environment where we can precisely measure individuals’ access to expertise, and where the institutional
4:130:10050:18:18:62:549:468:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:setting provides several sources of variation for causal identification. We hypothesize that members of a health
4:131:10162:18:18:62:549:450:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:professional’s extended family have informal access to health-related expertise, and that this may improve their
4:132:10274:18:18:62:549:432:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:investments into their own health capital. If so, then we may observe better health, and possibly lower mortality,
4:133:10388:18:18:62:342:414:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:among individuals with access to intra-family medical expertise.
4:134:10452:18:18:77:549:396:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Indeed, this is what we show in Section 4. We begin by comparing the mortality and health outcomes of
4:135:10553:18:17:62:549:378:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:individuals in families with and without a health professional in the raw data. We show that, conditional on
4:136:10661:17:18:62:549:361:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:individual income rank at age 55, individuals with a doctor or nurse in the extended family are more likely to
4:137:10771:18:18:62:549:343:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:survive until age 80 and less likely to suffer from chronic lifestyle-related conditions. Further, children with a
4:138:10885:18:18:62:549:325:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:health professional in the extended family are substantially more likely to have undertaken a preventive investment
4:139:11000:18:18:62:550:307:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:that we observe – HPV vaccination by age 20 – and less likely to have been exposed to tobaccoin utero.7These
4:140:11108:18:18:62:549:289:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:patterns in the raw data remain economically and statistically significant when we control non-parametrically for
4:141:11221:18:18:62:549:271:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:a wide range of observable demographics, in the spirit of the identification strategies pursued byBronnenberg et
4:142:11333:18:18:62:248:253:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:al. (2015) andJohnson and Rehavi(2016).
4:143:11372:18:18:77:549:235:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Comparing demographically equivalent individuals with and without a health professional in the extended
4:144:11475:18:18:62:549:217:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:family may still yield a biased estimate of the effect of intra-family access to expertise ifunobservables are
4:145:11585:18:18:62:549:199:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:correlated with this exposure, however.  To assuage these concerns, we also pursue two quasi-experimental
4:146:11690:18:18:62:549:181:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:approaches to identify causal effects. First, we leverage a set of medical school “admissions lotteries.” In Sweden,
4:147:11806:18:18:62:549:163:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:a centralized admission process usually generates sharp GPA thresholds for admission to any university program.
4:148:11917:18:14:62:549:145:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Due to substantial grade inflation (see, e.g.,Diamond and Persson,2016), the cutoff for all medical schools hit the
4:149:12032:14:12:73:549:131:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:5Data from the United States used in this comparison is reported by the Health Inequality Project https://healthinequality.org/.
4:150:12160:12:10:62:549:119:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:Also see Sjogren and Hartman (2018) for an analysis of how mortality inequality has evolved over time in Sweden. A large body of
4:151:12288:10:9:62:549:109:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:research on early-life health has documented that poor children are born less healthy than their advantaged counterparts; also, see,
4:152:12420:9:7:62:533:100:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:e.g., Currie and Moretti(2007) andRoyer(2009) for evidence of intergenerational correlations with early life health in the US.
4:153:12546:7:12:73:549:93:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:6The idea of considering factors other than formal access to healthcare is consistent with the largely mixed findings of a voluminous
4:154:12679:12:10:62:549:81:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:literature (mostly in US settings) that has investigated the causal effect of health insurance – which lowers the price and ease of
4:155:12810:10:9:62:77:71:8:g_d0_f6:6:g_d0_f5:F:access to formal healthcare – on long- and short-run health outcomes (Finkelstein et al.,2018b;Sommers et al.,2017).7
4:156:12927:9:0:77:346:62:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:A:We rank children by their parents’ household income percentile at birth.
5:157:13000:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:top GPA starting in 2002, and admission was randomized within the group of applicants with the highest possible
5:158:13111:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:GPA. Our identification strategy leverages this randomization, by comparing family members of applicants to
5:159:13218:18:18:62:446:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:medical school with a top GPA who were admitted and not admitted to medical school.
5:160:13301:18:18:77:549:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Our results from the lottery analysis are consistent with our non-parametric findings and show far-reaching
5:161:13408:18:17:62:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:health benefits for the admitted applicants’ extended family (including grandparents, parents, siblings, children,
5:162:13522:17:18:62:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:cousins, and in-laws). Among older relatives, access to intra-family expertise reduces the occurrence of lifestyle-
5:163:13637:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:related diseases and improves drug adherence. For example, eight years after the applicant’s matriculation, older
5:164:13750:18:18:62:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:relatives are 3 (5) percentage points less likely to have had a heart attack (heart failure), and 27% more likely to
5:165:13866:18:18:62:549:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:adhere to medication that can prevent heart attacks. Among younger relatives, access to intra-family expertise
5:166:13976:18:18:62:549:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:also raises preventive investments: adolescents are 20 percentage points more likely to be vaccinated against HPV
5:167:14089:18:18:62:500:540:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:by the age 25. Further, children have fewer inpatient stays, suggesting general health improvements.
5:168:14189:18:18:77:549:522:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:While the medical school lottery resembles an ideal experiment, this design only permits a relatively short
5:169:14296:18:18:62:549:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:follow-up period, as the lotteries were recent. This precludes studying outcomes such as mortality and the gradual
5:170:14410:18:18:62:549:486:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:onset of some lifestyle-related chronic conditions, as the parents of medical school applicants are relatively young
5:171:14526:18:18:62:549:468:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:(while grandparents are frequently already deceased). We therefore complement this analysis with a second quasi-
5:172:14638:18:18:62:549:450:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:experimental approach: event studies that compare individuals’ health before and after their (often younger)
5:173:14746:18:18:62:549:432:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:family member receives either a medical degreeor a law degree.8We find striking differences in the health and
5:174:14855:18:18:62:549:414:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:mortality profiles of the two groups in the raw data, and our results are confirmed in a rich regression specification
5:175:14973:18:18:62:549:396:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:that reveal little trends in health outcomes predating the arrival of a health professional or lawyer in the family.
5:176:15089:18:17:62:549:378:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:“Getting” a doctor in the family yields a 10% reduction in mortality 25 years after the doctor’s matriculation,
5:177:15200:17:18:62:549:361:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:along with substantially lower rates of heart attacks, heart failure, diabetes, and lung cancer.  These effects
5:178:15311:18:18:62:435:343:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:emerge gradually, which points to improved health behaviors over a long time period.
5:179:15395:18:18:77:549:325:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Despite the fact that the results from our three identification strategies are not directly comparable due to the
5:180:15508:18:18:62:549:307:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:different samples and time horizons, they deliver largely overlapping insights, which underscores their credibility.
5:181:15624:18:18:62:549:289:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:In sum, access to intra-family medical expertise improves physical health and raises investment in health capital,
5:182:15738:18:18:62:549:271:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:at all ages. Moreover, across all empirical approaches and outcomes, we find that the treatment effects are equal
5:183:15851:18:18:62:549:253:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:or more pronounced at the lower end of the income distribution, suggesting that the value of intra-family health
5:184:15963:18:18:62:214:235:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:expertise is larger among the poor.
5:185:15998:18:18:77:549:217:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Section 5 discusses the mechanism and the implications of our findings for health inequality. We find no
5:186:16102:18:18:62:549:199:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:evidence of income effects. Similarly, our results do not appear to stem from preferential treatment, e.g., through
5:187:16217:18:18:62:549:181:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:higher-cost procedures or faster care, which would come at the expense of patients who lack intra-family medical
5:188:16329:18:18:62:549:163:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:connections. Instead, intra-family transmission of health-related expertise increases preventive investments and
5:189:16441:18:18:62:549:145:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:induces behavioral changes that, from society’s perspective, are simple, cheap, and inherentlynot“zero-sum”: for
5:190:16553:18:18:62:549:127:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:example, adherence to low-cost but highly effective preventive drugs, take-up of universally accessible vaccines,
5:191:16666:18:14:62:267:109:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:and cessation of tobacco use during pregnancy.
5:192:16712:14:13:73:549:95:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:8The comparison of morbidity and mortality profiles at older ages between parents of doctors and lawyers is motivated by the
5:193:16836:13:9:62:549:82:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:fact that doctors and lawyers are both high-social status professions with similar income distributions; we verify that the parents of
5:194:16970:9:0:62:324:73:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:lawyers and doctors also have similar income distributions in the data.
6:195:17042:0:18:77:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:This, in turn, suggests that the benefits accruing to health professionals’ family members may, at least in
6:196:17149:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:part, be scalable through policies that mimic intra-family provision of expertise and promote these preventive
6:197:17259:18:18:62:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:investments and behavioral changes. What’s more, as we document weakly larger impacts of expertise at the
6:198:17364:18:18:62:549:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:lower end of the income distribution, such policies may have the potential to close part of the health-income gap
6:199:17477:18:17:62:198:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:(see, e.g., Lleras-Muney,2018).
6:200:17508:17:18:77:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:To explore this point, we use our results to create a “universal access to expertise” counterfactual. That is, we
6:201:17621:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:ask how the health-SES gradient would change if we gave everyone in society access to expertise. An input into
6:202:17731:18:18:62:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:this calculation, in addition to our estimated treatment effects, is the baseline distribution of access to expertise
6:203:17848:18:18:62:549:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:in society (in the absence of any policy intervention). Data from the European Social Survey shows that this
6:204:17956:18:18:62:549:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:distribution is skewed, with less expertise among low-SES individuals. Consequently, a larger share of low-SES
6:205:18066:18:18:62:517:540:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:individuals (than high-SES individuals) wouldgainexpertise under a universal expertise counterfactual.
6:206:18168:18:18:77:549:522:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Our back-of-the-envelope calculation suggests that providing universal access to expertise, and thereby equal-
6:207:18278:18:18:62:549:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:izing access to expertise across the income distribution, could close as much as 18% of the health inequality
6:208:18387:18:18:62:549:486:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:gap. While this universal expertise benchmark is instructive in its own right – not the least by emphasizing that
6:209:18500:18:18:62:549:468:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:unequal access to expertise can generate substantial health inequality, even in a setting with equalized access to
6:210:18614:18:18:62:549:450:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:health insurance – we close by discussing whether and how a policy maker may be able to mimic intra-family
6:211:18720:18:18:62:549:432:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:provision of expertise.  We speculate that such policies could be driven by both public and private entities,
6:212:18829:18:18:62:508:414:10:g_d0_f2:7:g_d0_f4:B:encompassing public health interventions as well as targeted design of private health insurance plans.9
6:213:18932:18:18:77:549:396:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Our work builds on and contributes to several strands of the literature. While a broad literature studies
6:214:19037:18:17:62:549:378:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the importance of the family as a source of insurance (see, e.g.,Lee and Persson,2016;Autor et al.,2017;
6:215:19141:17:18:62:549:361:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Persson,Forthcoming) or shocks (e.g.,Persson and Rossin-Slater,2018), a smaller body of work examines the
6:216:19246:18:18:62:549:343:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:importance of the family as a nexus for transmission of expertise, information, and norms. For example,Hvide
6:217:19354:18:18:62:549:325:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:and Oyer(2018) study parent-child communication of industry-specific knowledge, andBell et al.(2017) analyze
6:218:19462:18:18:62:549:307:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:parent-child transmission of know-how and norms relevant to innovation. We instead focus on familial transfers
6:219:19572:18:18:62:549:289:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of health-related expertise; further, we do not restrict attention to the the nuclear family, but analyze these
6:220:19683:18:18:62:242:271:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:processes in the broader extended family.
6:221:19724:18:18:77:549:253:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Our focus on health-related expertise relates the paper to the large and growing literature in many fields
6:222:19830:18:18:62:549:235:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:that analyzes the impact of information, broadly defined, on health behaviors, including the following most
6:223:19937:18:18:62:549:217:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:recent examples of studies:Hut and Oster(2018) analyze one particular but important health behavior – diet
6:224:20043:18:18:62:549:199:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:– and show that dietary habits fail to respond to an individual’s own disease diagnosis or to governmental diet
6:225:20154:18:18:62:549:181:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:recommendations.Fadlon and Nielsen(2017) study how individuals respond to a family member experiencing a
6:226:20258:18:15:62:549:163:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:sudden health shock (non-fatal heart attacks or strokes), finding that spouses and adult children increase their
6:227:20370:15:12:73:549:148:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:9To the extent that the power of intra-family communication about health stems from trust or detailed knowledge about the
6:228:20491:12:10:62:549:136:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:health history and habits that come with a relationship that spans a long period of time, effective policies may need to strive to
6:229:20621:10:9:62:549:126:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:mimic the depth of these relationships. One example of such a policy may be a nurse outreach program with a strong emphasis
6:230:20744:9:10:62:549:117:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:on the continuity of care (yielding along-termrelationship); further, Alsan et al. (2018) suggests that providers which resemble
6:231:20872:10:9:62:549:107:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:the patient (in their case, same-race providers) may gain more trust. Having a health professional in the family can essentially be
6:232:21003:9:10:62:549:98:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:thought of as one extreme on the spectrum between “unconnected” to the health care system and “connected within the family” on
6:233:21129:10:9:62:549:88:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:the other (the case that we study). Existing literature documents positive health impacts of interventions that lie “in between” on
6:234:21260:9:10:62:549:79:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:this spectrum, such as nurse home visiting programs (see, e.g.,Wüst,2012;Hjort et al.,2017) and community health care centers
6:235:21385:10:0:62:504:69:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:(see, e.g.,Bailey and Goodman-Bacon,2015). See Appendix SectionC for a more detailed discussion of this literature.
7:236:21501:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:consumption of preventive care (cholesterol-lowering medication) in response. Our results are consistent with
7:237:21610:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:theirs in that they underscore the importance of one’s family for models of health behaviors.  We explore a
7:238:21717:18:18:62:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:different mechanism, however: rather than salience of a health condition or the arrival of information about
7:239:21825:18:18:62:549:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:genetic disposition towards a disease, we analyze the role of spillovers from expert knowledge in the family. Our
7:240:21938:18:17:62:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:focus on expertise about health relates toJohnson and Rehavi(2016) who show that female physicians are less
7:241:22045:17:18:62:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:likely to receive a c-section when they themselves give birth, suggesting that their expertise on the health costs
7:242:22159:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of this procedure affects their own health care consumption, and toArtmann et al.(2019) who study healthcare
7:243:22267:18:18:62:321:594:10:g_d0_f2:7:g_d0_f4:B:use among parents of medical doctors in the Netherlands.10
7:244:22325:18:18:77:549:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:More generally, our findings contribute to the literature documenting a positive association between educa-
7:245:22432:18:18:62:549:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:tional attainment and own health and health behaviors (see, e.g.,Cutler and Lleras-Muney,2008;Cutler and
7:246:22536:18:18:62:549:540:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Lleras-Muney,2010;Meghir et al.,2018). Further,Currie and Moretti(2003) document positive spillovers of
7:247:22639:18:18:62:549:522:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:maternal education on child health as measured by birth weight.11We build on this literature by considering a
7:248:22748:18:18:62:495:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:precise type of education – a medical degree – and by analyzing spillovers across large family trees.
7:249:22849:18:18:77:549:486:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Finally, contrary to the papers cited above, on expertise and information broadly defined or on educational
7:250:22956:18:18:62:549:468:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:attainment in particular, we quantitatively explore the implications of our findings for the broader question
7:251:23065:18:18:62:550:450:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of the roots of health inequality, relating our work to a plethora of research on health inequality.12Here, we
7:252:23175:18:18:62:549:432:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:make two distinct contributions.  First, we deliver estimates of the health-income gradient and show that it
7:253:23283:18:18:62:549:414:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:steepens over time using comprehensive, non-self-reported data on both health outcomes and precise measures
7:254:23390:18:18:62:549:396:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of income.13Second, we provide quasi-experimental evidence on one particular causal mechanism underlying the
7:255:23498:18:41:62:509:378:10:g_d0_f2:7:g_d0_f4:B:health-income gradient, and show that it may play an important role in sustaining health inequality.14
7:256:23600:41:31:62:294:337:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:C:2  Institutional setting and data
7:257:23633:31:25:62:221:306:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:2.1  Healthcare in Sweden
7:258:23658:25:18:62:549:281:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Swedish healthcare is a textbook case of a universal health insurance system. The government runs a large public
7:259:23770:18:17:62:549:263:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:insurer and finances its expenditures from tax revenue. Coverage includes inpatient care, primary and specialty
7:260:23881:17:15:62:549:246:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:outpatient care, and prescription pharmaceuticals. Patients incur little out of pocket cost, paying at most a
7:261:23990:15:12:69:549:231:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:10Similarly, Bronnenberg et al.(2015) provide evidence on how expert knowledge among pharmacists affects their willingness to
7:262:24115:12:7:62:247:219:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:pay for branded (versus genetic) pharmaceuticals.
7:263:24164:7:12:69:549:212:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:11McCrary and Royer(2011) also establish a positive effect of maternal education on infant health. Further,Lundborg and Majlesi
7:264:24291:12:10:62:549:200:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:(2018) exploit a Swedish compulsory schooling reform to document spillovers in the opposite direction, from children’s education to
7:265:24422:10:7:62:375:190:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:parental longevity. Also seeKuziemko(2014) on intra-family spillovers of education.
7:266:24505:7:12:69:549:183:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:12See, e.g.,Adler et al.(1994) for a review of early evidence on a socioeconomic gradient in health and mortality andCurrie(2011)
7:267:24634:12:9:62:549:171:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:for a review of health inequality early in life. See also, e.g.,Fuchs(1992,2004),Cullen et al.(2012),National Academies of Sciences,
7:268:24766:9:10:62:549:162:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:Engineering, and Medicine(2015),The Future of Children(2015),Currie and Schwandt(2016),Seligman et al.(2016),Almond et
7:269:24884:10:9:62:76:152:8:g_d0_f6:6:g_d0_f5:F:al. (2017),Dwyer-Lindgren et al.(2017),Fuchs and Eggleston(2018), andThakrar et al.(2018).13
7:270:24976:9:10:77:549:143:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:The fact that the gradient weekly steepens throughout childhood and adolescence is consistent with evidence (using less granular
7:271:25104:10:9:62:549:133:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:measures of socioeconomic status) from the United States byCase et al.(2002), from Canada byCurrie and Stabile(2006), and
7:272:25225:9:7:62:241:124:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:from the United Kingdom byCase et al.(2008).
7:273:25269:7:12:69:549:117:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:14Our exercise relates to that ofAizer and Stroud(2010), who show that the arrival of novel information – in particular, the
7:274:25393:12:10:62:549:105:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:Surgeon General’s recommendation, made in 1964, that women should refrain from smoking during pregnancy – induced women
7:275:25512:10:9:62:549:95:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:with higher education to respond but elicited little response among mothers with lower educational attainment, thus increasing
7:276:25638:9:9:62:549:86:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:inequality at birth. Our findings, in contrast, suggest that intra-family expertise elicits a weakly larger response at the lower end of
7:277:25774:9:0:62:151:77:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:the income distribution.
8:278:25799:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:small co-pay.15Further, the public safety net reduces existing out of pocket obligations for some particularly
8:279:25909:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:vulnerable groups. Thus, in practice, individuals at any point in the income distribution have the same formal
8:280:26019:18:35:62:151:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:access to healthcare.
8:281:26040:35:24:62:121:648:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:2.2  Data
8:282:26049:24:18:62:549:624:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:For the universe of individuals living in Sweden over an extended time period, we use detailed mortality and
8:283:26157:18:18:62:549:606:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:medical records, matched to individual-level tax and educational records and a mapping of family trees spanning
8:284:26268:18:18:62:549:588:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:up to four generations.16Here, we describe the overall structure of the data; in subsequent sections, we define
8:285:26379:18:32:62:387:570:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the variables and sub-populations that we use in each part of the analysis.
8:286:26454:32:18:62:549:538:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f2:B:Overall sampleWe have data on the universe of individuals born between 1936 and 2016 that were living
8:287:26555:18:17:62:549:520:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:in Sweden in 1961 or at some later point in time. For these individuals, we know the exact year and month of
8:288:26663:17:18:62:549:503:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:birth, as well as the year of death (recorded starting with 1961 and up until 2017), and whether the individual
8:289:26774:18:18:62:549:485:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:was born in Sweden. From Statistics Sweden we obtain a file that connects each individual in this sample to the
8:290:26885:18:18:62:549:467:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:individual’s mother and father. Equipped with these data, we can connect all individuals born in 1936 or later to
8:291:26998:18:18:62:549:449:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:both their own parents, as well as to their siblings and descendants – children, nieces, nephews, and grandchildren.
8:292:27114:18:32:62:521:431:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Similarly, for later-born cohorts, these data allow us to identify parents, aunts, uncles, and grandparents.
8:293:27222:32:18:62:549:399:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f2:B:Socioeconomic informationWe merge these data to annual income tax records for the adult population (age
8:294:27325:18:18:62:549:381:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:16-74) over a 27-year time period, 1990 - 2016. These records contain detailed, third-party reported information
8:295:27437:18:18:62:549:363:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:about labor income, financial income, government transfers, as well as self-reported information about self-
8:296:27545:18:18:62:550:345:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:employment income. We use individual work and business income in our analysis.17The average individual
8:297:27647:18:18:62:549:327:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:pre-tax work and business income (among individuals with a positive income) in the last year of our data (2016)
8:298:27758:18:18:62:549:309:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:is 298,597 SEK ($34,878) with a standard deviation of 256,047 SEK. In the same database, we also observe
8:299:27862:18:18:62:549:291:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:educational attainment at an annual level, which allows us to know when individuals complete their degrees and
8:300:27972:18:31:62:182:273:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:which subject they studied.
8:301:27999:31:18:62:549:242:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f2:B:Healthcare recordsTo construct measures of health outcomes, health investments, and healtcare utilization
8:302:28104:18:18:62:549:224:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:throughout individuals’ lives, we merge in information from inpatient records, specialist outpatient care records,
8:303:28218:18:18:62:549:206:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:prescription drug records, and cause of death records.  Inpatient records cover years 1997 to 2016, specialist
8:304:28328:18:18:62:549:188:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:outpatient records years 2001 to 2016, and prescription drug records years 2005 to 2017. The inpatient records
8:305:28438:18:15:62:549:170:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:contain information on the universe of a patient’s visits to the hospital, including cases where the individual is
8:306:28552:15:12:69:549:155:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:15Once a patient’s out-of-pocket cost for medical care reaches SEK 1100 ($120) over a twelve month period, the co-pay is zero
8:307:28677:12:10:62:549:143:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:for all subsequent care during the remainder of the twelve-month period. Similarly, for prescription drugs, once ahousehold’s total
8:308:28808:10:9:62:549:133:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:out of pocket spending reaches SEK 2300 ($247) over a twelve month period, the co-pay is zero for all subsequent prescription fills
8:309:28939:9:10:62:549:124:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:during the remainder of the twelve-month period. For the purposes of calculating a household’s total out-of-pocket drug spending,
8:310:29068:10:9:62:76:114:8:g_d0_f6:6:g_d0_f5:F:a household is defined as one adult plus all children aged 18 or below that reside in the same abode.16
8:311:29171:9:7:77:438:105:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:A:Statistics Sweden provides detailed description of the administrative registry data at www.scb.se.
8:312:29269:7:12:69:549:98:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:17We examined several alternative measures of income, varying whether government transfers and investment income is included or
8:313:29396:12:9:62:549:86:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:excluded in the income measure. We did not find that our results were sensitive to these alternative specifications, as these variations
8:314:29532:9:0:62:163:77:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:tend to be rank-preserving.
9:315:29560:0:18:62:550:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:admitted and discharged on the same day. The outpatient data records all visitsoutside ofprimary care.18For
9:316:29667:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:each inpatient admission and outpatient specialist visit, the data contain rich information on the date of the visit,
9:317:29784:18:18:62:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the associated International Classification of Diseases (ICD-9 and ICD-10) diagnosis codes, procedure codes, and
9:318:29896:18:18:62:549:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the length of stay (for inpatient admissions). Drug records contain the universe of an individual’s prescription
9:319:30008:18:17:62:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:drug purchases made in pharmacies, but do not include over the counter drugs or drugs administered in hospitals.
9:320:30120:17:18:62:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:For each prescription drug purchase, the data contain the drug name, the active substance, the average daily
9:321:30228:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:dose, and the drug’s Anatomical Therapeutic Chemical (ATC) classification code. The ATC classification allows
9:322:30337:18:32:62:183:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:us to link drugs to diseases.
9:323:30366:32:18:62:549:562:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f2:B:Birth recordsWe further merge in complete medical birth records for the time period between 1995 to 2016,
9:324:30471:18:18:62:549:544:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:matching them to individual tax records. The birth records contain data on the month and year of birth, birth
9:325:30580:18:18:62:549:526:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:weight, birth length, head circumference, gestation (in days), and a variety of diagnosis codes at birth.  We
9:326:30689:18:18:62:549:508:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:also have variables from the electronic medical records related to pregnancy and delivery: tobacco use during
9:327:30798:18:18:62:549:490:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:pregnancy, pregnancy risk factors (diabetes, kidney disease, epilepsy, asthma, hypertension, or urinary infection),
9:328:30913:18:18:62:549:472:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the first date of prenatal care and the number of prenatal visits, caesarean section (c-section) delivery, induction
9:329:31029:18:32:62:329:454:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of labor, and the occurrence of any complications at delivery.
9:330:31091:32:18:62:550:422:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f2:B:Educational recordsFinally, we merge in educational records for year 2007 and onwards. There are two
9:331:31191:18:18:62:549:404:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:types of records. First, we use high school GPA information. This allows us to find medical school applicants
9:332:31300:18:17:62:549:386:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:with top GPAs, who would be competitive for randomized admission spots. Second, we use college application
9:333:31406:17:18:62:549:369:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:information. As college admissions in Sweden are centralized, we can observe the full set of programs to which
9:334:31516:18:18:62:549:351:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:each individual applies in each application cycle. We also observe admission outcomes, allowing us to track who
9:335:31627:18:42:62:299:333:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:gets admitted into (undergraduate) medical programs.
9:336:31679:42:28:62:298:291:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:C:3  Inequality in health: the facts
9:337:31713:28:18:62:549:263:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:We begin by documenting three robust stylized facts about health inequality in our setting: Health inequality
9:338:31822:18:18:62:549:245:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:emerges early in life, persists throughout adulthood, and is, at the end of life, as pronounced in Sweden as it
9:339:31933:18:18:62:549:227:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:is in the United States – despite Sweden’s universal health insurance and a generous social safety net. These
9:340:32042:18:18:62:549:209:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:facts underscore the importance of studying the role of factors other than social insurance in sustaining health
9:341:32154:18:32:62:452:191:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:inequality, and motivate our subsequent analysis of the importance of access to expertise.
9:342:32244:32:18:62:550:159:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f2:B:Inequality in mortalityTo study inequality in mortality, we start with all individuals that are alive at age
9:343:32352:18:18:62:549:141:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:55. These individuals are still several years away from retirement, allowing us to measure their work-related
9:344:32461:18:17:62:549:123:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:income, but are old enough to allow us to observe their deaths within our sample period. For each individual in
9:345:32572:17:16:62:549:106:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:this sample, we define an indicator for whether (s)he has died by age 80 – one of the key outcomes throughout
9:346:32681:16:12:69:549:90:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:18Primary care is provided at municipal “Care centrals” (Vårdcentraler); data from these centers has historically not been collected,
9:347:32814:12:9:62:549:78:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:limiting our ability to analyze individuals’ utilization of primary care, except for the case of care during pregnancy, which is recorded
9:348:32951:9:0:62:101:69:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:separately.
10:349:32963:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:our paper. Panel A of Figure1 plots the share of individuals that died by age 80 against individual income rank
10:350:33074:18:18:62:550:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:at age 55.19Despite Sweden’s generous social safety net and equalized formal access to health care, there is a
10:351:33184:18:18:62:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:strong gradient in cumulative mortality at older ages conditional on surviving to 55.20At the very bottom of
10:352:33292:18:18:62:549:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the income distribution, more than 40% have died by age 80; at the very top, the corresponding number is below
10:353:33402:18:17:62:83:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:25%.
10:354:33406:17:18:77:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:It is instructive to briefly put these numbers in relation to the income gradient in mortality that has recently
10:355:33518:18:18:62:550:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:been documented in the U.S.. Figure2 plots one-year log-mortality against own income rank in both countries,
10:356:33626:18:18:62:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:for three combinations of age at death and age of income measurement for which we were able to construct
10:357:33730:18:18:62:549:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:estimates that can can be directly compared to those reported for the U.S. inChetty et al.(2016). In the first
10:358:33840:18:18:62:549:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:two panels of Figure2, we plot log-mortality at age 75 against income rank at age 61 in the U.S. and age 60 for
10:359:33951:18:18:62:549:540:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Sweden (a year before the earliest retirement ages in the respective countries), separately for men (Panel A) and
10:360:34064:18:18:62:549:522:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:women (Panel B).21We observe substantially lower mortality, atanypoint in the relative income distribution, in
10:361:34174:18:18:62:549:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Sweden relative to the U.S., consistent with the notion that universal health insurance and a broad safety net may
10:362:34288:18:18:62:549:486:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:raise a society’s overall level of well-being; however, the slopes of the mortality gradients are nearly identical in
10:363:34405:18:18:62:549:468:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the two countries. The subsequent four panels of Figure2 plot log-mortality at ages 60 and 40, by gender, against
10:364:34518:18:18:62:549:450:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:(gender-cohort-specific) income rank ventile measured two years earlier. While mortality inequality estimated at
10:365:34630:18:18:62:549:432:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:earlier ages is lower in Sweden than in the U.S. – especially age-40 inequality among women – the Swedish data
10:366:34740:18:32:62:320:414:10:g_d0_f2:7:g_d0_f4:B:reveals a pronounced mortality gradient at all three ages.22
10:367:34800:32:17:62:549:382:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f2:B:Inequality in health outcomes in adulthoodTo measure inequality in health outcomes in adulthood,
10:368:34896:17:18:62:549:365:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:we start by defining indicators variables that capture any occurrence, at the individual level, of four common
10:369:35006:18:18:62:549:347:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:conditions that can be linked to lifestyle causes and that we can measure precisely in our data: heart attack,
10:370:35116:18:18:62:549:329:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:heart failure, lung cancer, and type 2 diabetes. PanelB of Figure1 displays the share of individuals aged 55 or
10:371:35227:18:18:62:549:311:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:older that have a history of being diagnosed with at least one of these conditions, against individual income rank
10:372:35341:18:18:62:549:293:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:at age 55. The panel displays a steep gradient in the presence of these lifestyle-related conditions in the adult
10:373:35454:18:18:62:549:275:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:population. Individuals at the bottom ventile of the income distribution are more than twice as likely to have at
10:374:35567:18:18:62:549:257:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:least one of these conditions (20 percent) than individuals at the top ventile (10 percent). The income gradient
10:375:35679:18:18:62:344:239:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:is strongly pronounced in each of the four underlying conditions.
10:376:35744:18:15:77:549:221:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:For younger adults – who do not have a high prevalence of the chronic conditions analyzed above – we
10:377:35844:15:12:69:549:206:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:19We use work-related income defined as the sum of income from employment-related activities as well as (positive) business income
10:378:35974:12:9:62:549:194:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:from self-employment. To calculate the individual’s income rank, we measure individual’s income at age 55, and rank individuals
10:379:36101:9:10:62:549:185:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:within birth cohort and gender. We use cohorts born in Sweden between 1936 and 1937, for whom we observe both income at age
10:380:36224:10:7:62:459:175:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:55 and survival until age 80. The shape of the gradient remains the same if we use household income rank.
10:381:36329:7:12:69:549:168:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:20We investigate, but do not separately report, mortality by gender.  Among men at the at the 5th percentile of the income
10:382:36451:12:9:62:549:156:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:distribution at age 55, 48 percent are no longer alive by age 80; among men at the 95th percentile, the corresponding share is 25
10:383:36580:9:10:62:549:147:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:percent. Female mortality is lower at all points in the income distribution, but we observe a very similar gradient. Women in the
10:384:36709:10:9:62:549:137:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:lowest 5 percent of the income distribution have a 11 percentage point lower probability of being alive than their most advantaged
10:385:36839:9:7:62:249:128:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:peers, 18 percent of whom are not alive by age 80.
10:386:36889:7:12:69:549:121:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:21For these comparisons, we adjust our income measure so that it corresponds to the U.S. (positive) Adjusted Gross Income (AGI)
10:387:37016:12:10:62:549:109:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:measure, as used in Chetty et al.(2016). In particular, we add capital-based income and non-disability government transfers; we
10:388:37143:10:9:62:76:99:8:g_d0_f6:6:g_d0_f5:F:continue excluding individuals with zero or negative income levels.22
10:389:37212:9:10:77:549:90:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:See Adler et al.(1994) for a review of early evidence of a socioeconomic gradient in mortality across different countries and a
10:390:37339:10:0:62:171:80:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:discussion of possible drivers.
11:391:37371:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:examine a measure of preventive health investments: HPV vaccination by age 20.23We report the gradient in
11:392:37476:18:18:62:550:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f3:B:HPV vaccination among females in Panel Cof Figure1. We now use a different x-axis: individuals’parental
11:393:37579:18:18:62:550:683:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f2:B:household incomerank in the year before the individual’s birth (i.e., 21 years earlier).24The solid triangles mark
11:394:37693:18:18:62:549:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:aggregate vaccination levels in our data, while the hollow circles are estimated separately for year 2007, which was
11:395:37809:18:17:62:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the first year the vaccine was available in Sweden. The figure shows a sharpreversegradient in this preventive
11:396:37919:17:18:62:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:health measure. Only about 10 percent of women born into households at the bottom of the income distribution
11:397:38027:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:get vaccinated against HPV, while 40 percent of women with parents at the top of the income distribution do. In
11:398:38138:18:18:62:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:2007, the first year that the vaccine was available in Sweden (right y-axis), the levels of vaccination are an order
11:399:38254:18:18:62:549:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of magnitude lower than in the aggregate data. The gradient is similar in shape, however, highlighting that young
11:400:38367:18:18:62:549:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:adults coming from more affluent households were much more likely to be early adopters of the new vaccine.
11:401:38473:18:18:62:549:540:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:This evidence of a gradient in the early adoption of a new medical technology is consistent with the argument in
11:402:38585:18:18:62:549:522:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Link and Phelan(1995) andCutler et al.(2006) that differential adoption of new medical technologies could be
11:403:38693:18:18:62:549:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:an important driver of health inequality. Our paper sheds light on a potential mechanism that could drive such
11:404:38803:18:32:62:163:486:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:differences in adoption.
11:405:38827:32:18:62:549:454:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f2:B:Early emergence of the health-SES gradientHaving documented pronounced gradients in mortality, adult
11:406:38927:18:18:62:549:436:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:health, and youth preventive investments in Sweden, we now investigate whether the gradient emerges already
11:407:39034:18:18:62:549:418:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:in early life. This can help formulate or reject hypotheses about the mechanisms that lead to the gradient, and
11:408:39145:18:18:62:506:400:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:also point to the most efficient timing of potential countervailing forces such as exposure to expertise.
11:409:39250:18:17:77:549:382:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:The lifestyle-related health outcomes analyzed above are rare early in life. Hence, to examine the extent of
11:410:39358:17:18:62:549:365:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the health gradient in childhood, we zoom in into one of the most common chronic conditions in childhood -
11:411:39464:18:18:62:549:347:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:asthma.25PanelA of Appendix FigureA1 reports the gradient. We define an indicator that turns on when
11:412:39564:18:18:62:549:329:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:children have a record of an asthma diagnosis in their inpatient or outpatient records at ages zero to five. We
11:413:39675:18:18:62:549:311:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:observe a substantially higher prevalence of asthma among children growing up in lower-SES households than
11:414:39781:18:18:62:253:293:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:among their more advantaged counterparts.
11:415:39822:18:18:77:549:275:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Further, to assess whether there is a gradient even earlier in life, we create two measures of the prenatal
11:416:39929:18:18:62:549:257:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:environment: an indicator for whether the mother is using tobacco right before or during pregnancy and an
11:417:40034:18:18:62:550:239:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:indicator for whether the child experiences a risky birth.26The gradient in tobacco use, depicted in PanelD
11:418:40141:18:18:62:549:221:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of Figure1, is remarkable, with more than 30 percent of mothers in the bottom income ventile using tobacco
11:419:40247:18:18:62:549:203:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:around the time of pregnancy, as compared to slightly above 5 percent of mothers at the top of the income
11:420:40352:18:18:62:549:185:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:distribution. Tobacco use and especially smoking is known to be associated with substantial risks to the fetus,
11:421:40463:18:18:62:549:167:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:including an increased risk of miscarriage, pre-term birth, and low birth weight (see, e.g.,Centers for Disease
11:422:40574:18:15:62:549:149:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Control and Prevention,2017); the steep gradient in tobacco exposure in-utero thus implies that babies born into
11:423:40686:15:9:69:445:134:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:A:23Human Papillomavirus (HPV) has been linked to several types of cancer, including cervical cancer.
11:424:40785:9:13:69:549:125:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:24To calculate parental household income rank at birth, we average two years of annual earnings of the child’s mother and father,
11:425:40914:13:9:62:549:112:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:measured one and two years before the child’s birth, respectively; sum them into household income; and rank households within each
11:426:41044:9:7:62:136:103:8:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f6:F:child’sbirth cohort.
11:427:41064:7:12:69:550:96:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:25Asthma is affecting nearly ten percent of all children in the United States (Chorniy et al.,2017); and in Sweden, already at age
11:428:41194:12:7:62:236:84:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:five roughly 11 percent are affected by asthma.
11:429:41241:7:12:69:549:77:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:26A risky birth is defined as whether the mother has any of the following conditions during pregnancy: chronic kidney diseases,
11:430:41368:12:0:62:541:65:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:diabetes, epilepsy, lung diseases, systemic lupus erythematosus (SLE), ulcerative colitis, hypertension, or urinary tract infections.
12:431:41502:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:disadvantaged households have received substantively lower health investments already before birth. Similarly,
12:432:41612:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:as shown in Panel B of Appendix FigureA1, adverse events at birth are more likely at the bottom of the income
12:433:41721:18:18:62:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:distribution than at the top,despitethe fact that mothers are almost eight years older at the top of the income
12:434:41832:18:18:62:473:665:10:g_d0_f2:7:g_d0_f4:B:distribution and the latent probability of a high risk pregnancy increases with maternal age.27
12:435:41927:18:17:77:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Finally, to track the evolution of the health gradient over the life cycle, we use a health measure that is
12:436:42034:17:18:62:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:relevant at all ages: the number of inpatient visits. PanelC of Appendix FigureA1 displays the gradient in the
12:437:42144:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:number of inpatient visits in the first five years of life. While we observe a pronounced gradient already at age
12:438:42257:18:18:62:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:5, it steepens substantially over the course of the life cycle, as illustrated in PanelD of the same figure, which
12:439:42371:18:18:62:316:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:displays the same outcome in the five years from 45 to 50.
12:440:42429:18:18:77:549:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:In sum, this section documents that the health-SES gradient emerges early in life and persists and gradually
12:441:42537:18:18:62:549:540:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:steepens throughout the life cycle – despite Sweden’s broad social safety net. This underscores the importance
12:442:42647:18:18:62:549:522:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of studying the role of factors other than social insurance in sustaining health inequality. In the remainder of
12:443:42759:18:42:62:545:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:this paper, we examine one such potential piece of the puzzle: differential exposure to health-related expertise.
12:444:42872:42:31:62:373:462:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:C:4  Access to expertise and health outcomes
12:445:42914:31:24:62:309:431:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:4.1  Measuring access to health expertise
12:446:42955:24:18:62:549:407:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:We are interested in measuring whether access to health-related expertise affects individuals’ investments into
12:447:43066:18:18:62:549:389:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:their health and their subsequent health outcomes. Access to expertise may affect individuals through multiple
12:448:43176:18:18:62:549:371:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:mechanisms. Experts can transmit new knowledge about the costs and benefits of healthy behaviors and health
12:449:43283:18:18:62:549:353:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:investments, or they can remind, nudge or corroborate existing knowledge, making it more salient and trustworthy.
12:450:43396:18:18:77:549:335:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:While it is intuitive that exposure to any or all of these underlying mechanisms may lead to more health
12:451:43500:18:18:62:549:317:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:investments and better health outcomes (indeed, the provision of knowledge has traditionally been one of the
12:452:43608:18:18:62:549:299:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:most common policy instruments), investigating the causal role of access to expertise is challenging.  First,
12:453:43717:18:18:62:549:281:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:individuals receive streams of information and reminders relevant to their health from many differences sources
12:454:43828:18:17:62:549:263:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:throughout their lifetime, and these flows may be hard to measure; second, exposure to expertise is typically
12:455:43937:17:18:62:549:246:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:not randomly assigned. To overcome these challenges, we zoom in into an environment where we can precisely
12:456:44043:18:18:62:549:228:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:measure individuals’ exposure to expertise, and where the institutional environment provides several sources of
12:457:44154:18:18:62:457:210:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:variation for causal identification: the presence of a health professional (HP) in the family.
12:458:44248:18:18:77:549:192:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Having an HP in the family can affect individuals’ health in a variety of ways, which we can broadly classify
12:459:44357:18:18:62:549:174:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:into two distinct channels. First – and this is our channel of interest – having an HP in the family is likely
12:460:44467:18:18:62:549:156:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:to increase access to health-related expertise in the familial environment. This “access to expertise” channel
12:461:44577:18:18:62:549:138:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:encompasses transmission of (new) health-related knowledge to family members in a variety of informal settings;
12:462:44688:18:18:62:549:120:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:as well as reminding family members to invest into their health by undertaking beneficial health behaviors,
12:463:44795:18:15:62:549:102:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:avoiding harms, adhering to medications, and doing regular check-ups. Second, having an HP in the family may
12:464:44903:15:12:69:549:87:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:27The lowest rate of adverse events, however, occurs in the middle of the income distribution, where mothers are have access to
12:465:45030:12:0:62:229:75:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:more resources, but are still relatively young.
13:466:45079:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:affect health through what we call the “access to care” channel: this, in turn, encompasses a variety of ways in
13:467:45191:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:which individuals may leverage the intra-family social capital and connections to the health care system to get
13:468:45302:18:18:62:319:683:10:g_d0_f2:7:g_d0_f4:B:better (for example, more expensive) or faster treatment.28
13:469:45361:18:18:77:549:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Throughout our analysis, we are interested in investigating the importance of the “access to expertise” channel,
13:470:45473:18:17:62:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:for two reasons. First, increasing access to health-related expertise in the population is fundamentally a scalable
13:471:45588:17:18:62:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:public policy. (In Appendix Section C, we review the extensive literature on several existing interventions that at
13:472:45703:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:their core all aim to increase health-related expertise in the population, such as nurse outreach programs, efforts
13:473:45818:18:18:62:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:to improve the continuity of primary care, and public health campaigns against smoking or for cancer screening.)
13:474:45930:18:18:62:549:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:The “access to care” channel in contrast, is fundamentally not scalable, as it implies individuals with family
13:475:46040:18:18:62:549:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:connections in the health care system getting ahead of those lacking such connections. This makes any policy
13:476:46148:18:18:62:549:540:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:that increases access to care, holding the total amount of healthcare resources fixed, a zero sum policy. Second,
13:477:46261:18:18:62:549:522:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:historically, the “extensive” margin of disease prevention through changes in social and individual investments
13:478:46372:18:18:62:549:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:into health - that we hypothesize can be affected by access to health expertise - has had a larger effect on
13:479:46480:18:18:62:549:486:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:population health than the “intensive” margin of moving from a lower to a higher quality of care provider, or
13:480:46589:18:18:62:389:468:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:getting care faster within a given system (Cutler and Lleras-Muney,2008).
13:481:46662:18:18:77:549:450:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:In this section, we analyze the impact of having a health professional on the extended family’s health; we
13:482:46768:18:18:62:549:432:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:then return to a discussion about the mechanism in Section5.1 – there, we present evidence consistent with the
13:483:46878:18:35:62:368:414:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:“access to expertise” channel being an important driver of our results.
13:484:46949:35:24:62:240:379:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:4.2  Non-parametric evidence
13:485:46977:24:18:62:549:355:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:We use the records of higher education to find individuals with health professional degrees - physicians and nurses
13:486:47092:18:18:62:350:337:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:- among the cohorts of working age adults in our analytic sample.
13:487:47157:18:18:77:549:319:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:We define two groups of individuals who may benefit from (differential degrees of) access to expertise: the
13:488:47264:18:18:62:549:301:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:health professionals’narrowandextendedfamilies, respectively.  The narrow family is defined as the health
13:489:47369:18:18:62:549:283:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:professional’s spouse, parents, parents-in-law, children, and children-in-law. The extended family further includes
13:490:47484:18:18:62:404:265:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the health professional’s siblings, aunts and uncles, grandparents, and cousins.
13:491:47564:18:17:77:549:247:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:We start by documenting differences in health between individuals in families with and without a health
13:492:47667:17:18:62:549:230:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:professional. Panel3A of Figure3 revisits the mortality gradient from Figure1A, but now plots it separately for
13:493:47778:18:18:62:549:212:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:individuals with and without a health professional in theextendedfamily.29We drop observations for individuals
13:494:47888:18:18:62:292:194:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:who are educated as health professionals themselves.
13:495:47940:18:18:77:549:176:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Panel3A reveals two clear patterns in the raw data. First, there is a visually detectable difference in the
13:496:48047:18:15:62:549:158:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:probability of being alive at age 80, which persists throughout the income distribution: Conditional on income
13:497:48157:15:12:69:549:143:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:28Interestingly, in their ongoing workArtmann, Oosterbeek and van der Klaauw(2019) are finding - in the Dutch setting - that
13:498:48281:12:10:62:549:131:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:having a physician in the family in factdoes notresult in substantially increased access to care (on the contrary, it sometimes leads
13:499:48414:10:9:62:76:121:8:g_d0_f6:6:g_d0_f5:F:to less use), neither in terms of the quantity nor in terms of the price of care.29
13:500:48497:9:10:77:549:112:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:Recall that the x-axis is the percentile of the individuals’ age-55 work income rank, where work income includes wage income
13:501:48621:10:9:62:549:102:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:and self-employment income, but excludes government transfers and capital income. Our results are not sensitive to whether we
13:502:48746:9:9:62:549:93:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:include or exclude the other two sources of income. We use work income in our preferred specifications, as intuitively this is a broader
13:503:48882:9:10:62:549:84:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:measure of socio-economic status, pre redistribution programs. We restrict the sample to individuals with positive work income.
13:504:49009:10:9:62:549:74:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:As we condition on work income, we implicitly condition on being alive at age 55. Our results are also not sensitive to replacing
13:505:49138:9:0:62:257:65:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:individual income rank with household income rank.
14:506:49190:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:rank, individuals with an extended relative who is educated as a physician or a nurse are more likely to survive
14:507:49302:18:18:62:472:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:to age 80. Second, this mortality difference is larger at the bottom of the income distribution.
14:508:49398:18:18:77:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:We estimate the magnitude of the difference in cumulative mortality by age 80 at each income decile using
14:509:49503:18:21:62:200:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the following OLS specification:
14:510:49535:21:0:242:262:644:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f11:?:Yi=
14:511:49538:0:25:262:278:657:7:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f13:?:d=10∑
14:512:49543:25:0:264:278:632:7:g_d0_f10:7:g_d0_f12:?:d=1
14:513:49546:0:30:283:549:644:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f2:A:δd(i)HPi+βXi+-i(1)
14:514:49564:30:18:62:549:614:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Here,Yiis the mortality (or health) outcome of interest for individuali,HPiis an indicator variable that takes
14:515:49674:18:18:62:549:596:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the value of1if individualihas at least one medical professional in the family, andXiis a set of demographic
14:516:49782:18:18:62:549:578:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:controls that are included in some specifications. The first term is a sum of indicators for having a medical
14:517:49891:18:18:62:549:560:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:professional in the family interacted with income rank deciles. The coefficients of interest areδd(i)that measure
14:518:50004:18:18:62:549:542:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the average difference in the health outcome between individuals with and without a health professional in the
14:519:50114:18:18:62:549:524:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:extended family, for each age-55 income deciled(i). We report the results of this regression in Panel3B. The
14:520:50222:18:18:62:549:506:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:dashed line reports the estimates ofδd(i)without any controls; thus, these estimates measure the raw vertical
14:521:50331:18:18:62:549:488:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:distance between the two plotted lines in Panel1A. We estimate that, on average, individuals that have at least
14:522:50442:18:18:62:549:470:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:one extended family member who is a doctor or a nurse are 5.9 percentage points less likely to have died by
14:523:50549:18:18:62:549:452:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the age of 80 conditional on being alive at age 55. This is a large difference relative to the average probability
14:524:50663:18:18:62:549:434:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of having died by age 80 in the full sample, which is 31 percent, as it implies an 19 percent reduction in the
14:525:50773:18:17:62:549:416:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:probability of death. This is equivalent in magnitude to moving from the 70th to 100th percentile in the income
14:526:50884:17:18:62:549:399:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:rank distribution. Further, the difference varies by income rank, ranging from 7 percentage points on average in
14:527:50996:18:18:62:467:381:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the lower half of the distribution to 4 percentage points in the upper half of the distribution.
14:528:51092:18:18:77:549:363:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Next, we examine whether these differences remain when controlling non-parametrically for a wide range
14:529:51194:18:18:62:549:345:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of observable demographics, in the spirit of the identification strategies pursued byBronnenberg et al.(2015)
14:530:51303:18:18:62:549:327:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:and Johnson and Rehavi(2016). The solid line in Panel3B, as well as Panel A of Table1, report results from
14:531:51409:18:18:62:549:309:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:regression equation (1) including the vector of observablesXi.30The pattern remains qualitatively the same
14:532:51515:18:18:62:549:291:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:across all income deciles: Individuals with a health professional in the family are less likely to have died by age
14:533:51630:18:18:62:437:273:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:80, and the difference is on average larger at the lower end of the income distribution.
14:534:51718:18:18:77:549:255:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:We now revisit the prevalence of chronic conditions that are commonly considered to be linked to lifestyle
14:535:51824:18:18:62:549:237:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:decisions throughout the life-cycle. In panelC of Figure3 we report differences in the probability of having
14:536:51932:18:18:62:549:219:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the following conditions: heart attack, heart failure, type II diabetes, and lung cancer, by whether or not an
14:537:52042:18:18:62:549:201:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:individual has a health professional in the extended family. The conditions are aggregated into a z-score index.
14:538:52154:18:18:62:549:183:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:The raw data again shows a visible separation in the prevalence of these chronic conditions between individuals
14:539:52265:18:18:62:549:165:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:with and without a health professional in their extended families. As the dashed line in PanelD suggests, the
14:540:52374:18:17:62:549:147:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:differences in the raw data are larger at the bottom of the income distribution.  Moreover, less than 50% of
14:541:52482:17:18:62:549:130:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the difference can be explained by our rich set of observables, leaving us with a clear pattern (solid line) of
14:542:52593:18:18:62:549:112:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:significantly lower prevalence of lifestyle-related conditions among older individuals with health professionals in
14:543:52708:18:15:62:549:94:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:their families. As Panel B in Table1 documents, the difference remains on average larger at lower income levels.
14:544:52820:15:12:69:549:79:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:30The vector of controls includes fixed effects for: own income rank percentile, highest-earning relative’s income percentile, year
14:545:52951:12:0:62:436:67:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:of birth, gender, individual’s (discretized) educational attainment, and county of residence at age 55.
15:546:53056:0:18:77:550:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Figure 4 reports similar analyses for younger ages. In PanelsA and B we examine the probability of young
15:547:53160:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:women receiving the HPV vaccine by age 20. We observe large differences in the probability of these health
15:548:53266:18:18:62:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:investments across young adults with and without a health professional in the family, across all points in the
15:549:53376:18:18:62:549:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:income distribution. About two thirds of the differences persist when we control for observable characteristics,
15:550:53488:18:17:62:440:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:as can be seen in Panel C in Table1 as well as in the solid line in PanelB of Figure4.
15:551:53574:17:18:77:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f3:A:Finally, panels4C and4D report the same analysis for the probability of being exposed to tobacco usein
15:552:53676:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f2:B:utero. We observe large differences in tobacco exposure rates for an unborn child in families with and without
15:553:53786:18:18:62:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:a health professional (including the mother of the child herself), especially at the lower deciles of the income
15:554:53898:18:18:62:549:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:distribution.31A child with parents in the first two deciles of the income distribution who has a health professional
15:555:54015:18:18:62:549:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:in the family is up to 8 percentage points less likely to have been prenatally exposed to tobacco than a child
15:556:54125:18:18:62:549:540:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:who has no medical professionals in the family. As Panel4D and Panel D in Table1 document, the gap in
15:557:54226:18:18:62:549:522:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:tobacco exposure rates monotonically declines with income rank and gets close to a precise zero at the top of the
15:558:54339:18:18:62:549:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:income distribution. While a substantial portion of the differences can be attributed to differences in observable
15:559:54453:18:18:62:549:486:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:demographics, observables do not account for the full gap, leaving a significant discrepancy of up to nearly 5
