15:560:54563:18:18:62:549:468:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:percentage points (or 14%) at the lower end of the income distribution (Panel D in Table1). Further, observable
15:561:54674:18:18:62:532:450:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:differences cannot fully explain the pattern of a monotonically increasing gap with declining a income rank.
15:562:54782:18:18:77:549:432:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Figures5 and 6 examine the heterogeneity in our non-parametric results along the intensive margin of exposure
15:563:54891:18:18:62:549:414:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:to a health professional in the family. We examine two dimensions of heterogeneity: geographic proximity, and
15:564:55000:18:18:62:549:396:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:proximity along the family tree. The left-hand side panels in Figures5 and 6 report the estimated differences in
15:565:55112:18:17:62:549:378:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:health outcomes between: (i) individuals with a health professional in their broad (but not narrow) family and
15:566:55222:17:18:62:549:361:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:those individuals without any health professional relative (dashed lines); as well as (ii) between individuals with a
15:567:55339:18:18:62:549:343:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:health professional in their narrow family and those without any health professional (solid line). The differences
15:568:55453:18:18:62:549:325:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:in health outcome at each point in the income rank distribution are reported from the OLS regressions with the
15:569:55563:18:18:62:549:307:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:full set of controls as in PanelsB,  D of Figure3, as well as the respective Panels in Figure4). The right-hand
15:570:55674:18:18:62:549:289:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:side panels report the same analysis, but now splitting the sample by geographically close (solid line) and far
15:571:55785:18:18:62:549:271:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:(dashed line) health professional relatives. We define two family members as being geographically close if they
15:572:55896:18:18:62:541:253:10:g_d0_f2:7:g_d0_f4:B:have lived in the same county for more than 50% of the time during which they are observed in the sample.32
15:573:56003:18:18:77:549:235:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:We consistently find - for both older and younger relatives - that the effects of a health professional in
15:574:56109:18:18:62:549:217:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the family are substantially more pronounced if the health professional is a close relative. The differences are
15:575:56221:18:18:62:549:199:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:especially clear when zooming in onto the lower part of the income distribution. For example, at lower income
15:576:56330:18:18:62:549:181:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:rungs, having a health professional relative who is farther away along the family tree has very little effect on the
15:577:56446:18:18:62:549:163:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:prevalence of lifestyle-related conditions after age 55 (PanelC), while the effect is very pronounced for having a
15:578:56560:18:18:62:549:145:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:close relative who is a health professional. These results are intuitive, as we would expect the communication
15:579:56670:18:14:62:549:127:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:about health to be both more frequent and more open among closer family members.  The results are more
15:580:56772:14:13:69:549:113:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:31Notably, we find even larger differences when we consider only (children of) expecting mothers that are healthcare professionals
15:581:56902:13:9:62:549:100:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:themselves. There is almostno gradientin the probability of tobacco exposurein uteroamong children of these mothers, with a
15:582:57025:9:10:62:549:91:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:level difference of up to minus 20 percentage points relative to the general population. FigureA2 in the Appendix illustrates this
15:583:57155:10:9:62:76:81:8:g_d0_f6:6:g_d0_f5:F:striking difference.32
15:584:57177:9:9:77:549:72:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:County (“län”) is the top level geographic division in Sweden, with 21 counties as of 2019. The largest county (Stockholm) has
15:585:57303:9:0:62:372:63:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:2.3 million individuals, while the smallest (Gotland) has about 59 thousand people.
16:586:57388:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:mixed for geographic proximity.  We observe in FigureB that the mortality effect at the lower rungs of the
16:587:57494:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:income distribution is almost entirely driven by geographically close relatives, while the effects are similar at
16:588:57607:18:18:62:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:higher income rungs. For lifestyle-related diseases, there is almost no difference in the effects of having a health
16:589:57723:18:18:62:549:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:professional relative who lives far or nearby. For young children, the family tree and geographic proximity are
16:590:57834:18:17:62:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:often hard to separate, as children are likely to live in the same household as a close relative. In both cases,
16:591:57946:17:18:62:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:however, we find that HPV vaccination is more pronounced among young adults exposed to a health professional
16:592:58054:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:who is either a close family member or lives close by. For tobacco exposure, there is little difference on either
16:593:58167:18:18:62:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of the intensive margins at the top of the income distribution, while the intensity of exposure appears more
16:594:58275:18:18:62:549:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:important at the bottom of the income distribution. These results suggest that intensity of access to expertise is
16:595:58389:18:18:62:549:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:crucial for health production. Frequent communication with close family members generates consistent two-way
16:596:58497:18:18:62:549:540:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:information flows that are typically not present and not emphasized in the interactions within a formal healthcare
16:597:58611:18:18:62:94:522:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:system.
16:598:58618:18:18:77:549:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:While we control flexibly for a wide range of individual characteristics in this analysis, akin to the identification
16:599:58735:18:18:62:549:486:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:strategies pursued byBronnenberg et al.(2015) andJohnson and Rehavi(2016), a remaining concern is that
16:600:58837:18:18:62:549:468:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the presence of an HP in the family may be correlated withunobservables. We therefore use two additional
16:601:58941:18:18:62:549:450:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:identification strategies to quantify the causal impact on health and longevity of having a health professional in
16:602:59055:18:35:62:151:432:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the extended family.
16:603:59075:35:24:62:418:397:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:4.3  Leveraging randomization in medical school admissions
16:604:59133:24:18:62:549:373:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Our second research design exploits the fact that admission to medical school in Sweden, for a subset of years,
16:605:59244:18:18:62:549:355:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:contained an element of randomization.33“Medical school” in the Swedish context refers to an undergraduate
16:606:59350:18:18:62:549:337:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:major in medicine - medical training starts directly in college and not in a post-graduate professional school.
16:607:59461:18:18:62:549:319:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Students choose their undergraduate majors before starting higher education, apply to specific departments, and
16:608:59572:18:18:62:297:301:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:follow a curriculum recommended by the department.
16:609:59622:18:18:77:549:283:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f3:A:University applications in Sweden are centralized and handled by a governmental agency,Universitets- och
16:610:59726:18:18:62:549:265:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f2:B:högskolerådet(henceforth UHR). All prospective students interested in studying for all degrees and at all uni-
16:611:59836:18:17:62:549:247:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:versities apply through the same system. There are two university application cycles per year, for programs
16:612:59943:17:18:62:549:230:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:starting in the fall and spring semesters, respectively. In each application cycle, a prospective student submits a
16:613:60058:18:18:62:549:212:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:rank ordered list of programs to the UHR. The applicant is not required to apply to programs only in the same
16:614:60167:18:18:62:549:194:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:discipline. For example, an applicant may rank the medical school program at the Karolinska Institute in Stock-
16:615:60278:18:18:62:549:176:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:holm as her first alternative, the medical school program at Gothenburg University as her second alternative, a
16:616:60389:18:18:62:391:158:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:program in business at Lund University as her third alternative, and so on.
16:617:60464:18:18:77:549:140:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:The centralized agency allocates the bulk of the applicants to programs by ranking them by their high-school
16:618:60572:18:15:62:550:122:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:GPA.34The applicant with the highest GPA gets her preferred choice, the second highest ranked applicant gets
16:619:60680:15:12:69:549:107:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:33There are no tuition fees for post-secondary education in Sweden. To cover living expenses, most students are eligible for financial
16:620:60814:12:7:62:373:95:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:support (part loan/part grant) from The Swedish Board of Student Finance (CSN).
16:621:60893:7:12:69:549:88:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:34There are also other quotas allocating applicants. The most important of these alternative quotas is the one allocating applicants
16:622:61025:12:9:62:549:76:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:to slots based on their scores on the Swedish Scholastic Aptitude Test (SSAT, in Swedishhögskoleprovet). In addition, five years of
16:623:61156:9:0:62:270:67:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:work experience can add some extra points to the GPA.
17:624:61211:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the highest available choice for which she qualifies, and so on. For competitive programs, in which demand exceeds
17:625:61325:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:supply, this process generates GPA admission cutoffs for each program, around which admission is effectively
17:626:61433:18:18:62:115:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:randomized.
17:627:61444:18:18:77:549:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:The high school GPA ranges from 0.0 to 20.0. Since the inception of this grading system in 1997, grade
17:628:61546:18:17:62:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:inflation has been substantial (see, e.g.,Diamond and Persson,2016). The share of students graduating from
17:629:61652:17:18:62:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:high school with a GPA of 20.0 increased from less than 0.1 percent in 1997 to 0.8 percent in 2008 (Vlachos,2010)
17:630:61765:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:– an increase of more than 800 percent. As a consequence, many university programs saw their GPA admission
17:631:61871:18:18:62:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:cutoffs steadily increase over time. For medical school programs, which generally have the highest cutoffs of any
17:632:61984:18:18:62:549:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:programs in Sweden, this process eventually led to the cutoff hitting the 20.0 mark at all of Sweden’s medical
17:633:62094:18:18:62:95:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:schools.
17:634:62102:18:18:77:549:540:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Figure7 displays the maximum, minimum, and median GPA cutoffs for admissions to Sweden’s six medical
17:635:62202:18:18:62:549:522:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:schools from 1998 to 2017.35Prior to the fall 2002 application cycle, the admission cutoffs were gradually
17:636:62308:18:18:62:549:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:increasing over time, with slightly higher cutoffs in the fall than in the spring (reflecting the fact that more
17:637:62420:18:18:62:549:486:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:students apply right after graduating high school in the preceding summer). Starting in the fall of 2002 and
17:638:62528:18:18:62:549:468:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:during the subsequent fifteen application cycles (until the spring of 2010), both the highest and the lowest cutoffs
17:639:62644:18:18:62:549:450:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:were 20.0. Thus, admission to any medical school in the country necessitated the highest possible GPA of 20.0,
17:640:62754:18:18:62:549:432:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:and the admission wasrandomizedby the UHR within this group. Our primary identification strategy leverages
17:641:62860:18:18:62:549:414:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:this randomization, by comparing applicants to medial school with a GPA of 20.0 who were admitted and not
17:642:62965:18:18:62:191:396:10:g_d0_f2:7:g_d0_f4:B:admitted to medical school.36
17:643:62994:18:17:77:549:378:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:While the randomization of students with 20.0 into admission resembles a perfect RCT, one aspect of the
17:644:63097:17:18:62:549:361:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:institutional context complicate our analysis. Applicants who are not admitted on their first attempt, have the
17:645:63208:18:18:62:549:343:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:option of re-applying in subsequent application cycles.37The possibility of re-application implies that individuals
17:646:63323:18:18:62:549:325:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:that are not admitted in a particular cycle may still eventually gain admission and become physicians; thus, even
17:647:63436:18:18:62:549:307:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:conditional on a GPA of 20.0, being lotteried in or out is not a “sharp” allocation of students to medical schools.
17:648:63551:18:18:62:549:289:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:At the same time, not all students who are declined admission in their first application round choose to reapply.
17:649:63664:18:18:62:549:271:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Instead, they may choose to pursue other professions. Thus, being admitted on the applicant’s first application
17:650:63775:18:18:62:549:253:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:cycle (which is effectively random) affects the probability of the applicants eventually matriculating into a medical
17:651:63892:18:18:62:101:235:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:program.
17:652:63900:18:18:77:549:217:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Given this, we exploit admission on the student’sfirstapplication attempt an instrument for whether an
17:653:64002:18:18:62:549:199:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:individual eventually becomes a medical student and ultimately graduates with a medical degree. We proceed
17:654:64108:18:18:62:549:181:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:by estimating the following two stage least squares (2SLS) relationship (and the associated intent to treat (ITT)
17:655:64221:18:18:62:120:163:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:relationship):
17:656:64235:18:14:228:549:145:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f2:A:Yj(i)=δMDi+β1xj(i)+κ1Xi+-1(2)
17:657:64264:14:12:69:549:131:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:35Sweden has six medical schools during the time period for which we observe admissions data, with a seventh added in 2010 (in
17:658:64390:12:10:62:549:119:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:Örebro). In the years when not all schools’ cutoffs are 20.0, the highest admission cutoff is typically to the Karolinska Institute in
17:659:64524:10:9:62:76:109:8:g_d0_f6:6:g_d0_f5:F:Stockholm or to Lund University.36
17:660:64558:9:10:77:549:100:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:Randomization is not common, but is present in multiple higher education settings across different countries. SeeKetel et al.
17:661:64683:10:9:62:549:90:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:(2016) on the economic return to medical school admission lotteries in the Netherlands, as well asStasz and von Stolk(2007) on the
17:662:64813:9:7:62:227:81:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:overview of lottery use in multiple countries.
17:663:64859:7:12:69:549:74:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:37While waiting for the next application cycle, applicants may try to increase their admission chances, either by taking the scholastic
17:664:64994:12:0:62:380:62:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:aptitude test and attempting admission through the alternative quota, or by working.
18:665:65080:0:27:232:549:719:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f2:A:MDi=γAi+β2xj(i)+κ2Xi+-2(3)
18:666:65106:27:18:77:549:692:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:In equation (2),Yj(i)is the health outcome of interest for applicanti’s family memberj(we consider all
18:667:65208:18:18:62:550:674:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:members of the extended family, as discussed above).MDiis an indicator variable that takes the value of 1 if
18:668:65316:18:18:62:549:656:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:applicantimatriculated into a medical program.Xiandxj(i)are vectors of observable demographics of applicant
18:669:65423:18:17:62:500:638:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f2:B:iand his or her family memberj(i); these are not necessary for identification but improve precision.
18:670:65523:17:18:77:549:621:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:The demographic covariates for the applicant and family member, respectively, include year of birth fixed
18:671:65628:18:18:62:549:603:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:effects, a gender dummy, and an indicator for whether the individual was born in Sweden. All regressions also
18:672:65737:18:18:62:549:585:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:include fixed effects for the type of relative thatj(i)is to applicanti(grandparent, parent, child, aunt or uncle,
18:673:65851:18:18:62:549:567:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:sibling, sibling’s child, or cousin), and for family memberj(i)’s own level of education. Further, we control for
18:674:65964:18:18:62:549:549:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the number of medical schools the individualiapplies to in the first application round, as this mechanically
18:675:66072:18:18:62:286:531:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:affects the probability of admission (toaprogram).
18:676:66122:18:18:77:549:513:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:The coefficient of interest in equation (2) isδ, which measures the effect on health outcomes of having a
18:677:66227:18:18:62:549:495:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:family member get medical training. This coefficient may be biased if individuals whose relatives are in worse
18:678:66337:18:18:62:549:477:10:g_d0_f2:7:g_d0_f10:B:(or better) health systematically select into medical training. To address this concern, we instrument forMDi
18:679:66446:18:18:62:549:459:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:withAias specified in equation (3).Aitakes the value of1if studentiwas admitted to medical school in the
18:680:66550:18:18:62:550:441:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:first application cycle. The resulting estimate ofδmeasures the effect of having a family member initiate medical
18:681:66663:18:18:62:549:423:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:school for the group of compliers (LATE). Here, the compliers are family members of applicants who went to
18:682:66769:18:18:62:549:405:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:medical school because they won admission in their first application cycle, but who would not have matriculated
18:683:66880:18:18:62:516:387:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:in a medical school had they lost this first lottery. The standard errors are clustered at the family level.
18:684:66988:18:17:77:549:369:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:We observe ten years of complete application and admissions records, starting in the fall of 2007 and ending
18:685:67096:17:18:62:549:352:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:in the Spring of 2016. Our baseline sample of applicants includes all applicants to medical school in Sweden
18:686:67204:18:18:62:549:334:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:up until the spring of 2010 (when the cutoff score was 20.0), who had a GPA of exactly 20.0. Our sample of
18:687:67310:18:18:62:549:316:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:family members include all their grandparents, parents, parents-in-law, spouses, own children, aunts and uncles,
18:688:67422:18:18:62:233:298:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:siblings, siblings’ children, and cousins.
18:689:67464:18:18:77:549:280:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Table 2 displays the mean of observable baseline demographics as well the probability of matriculating into
18:690:67571:18:18:62:549:262:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:medical studies for two groups of applicants: those who were admitted (188 applicants) and those who were
18:691:67676:18:18:62:549:244:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:not admitted (555 applicants) in their first application cycle. First, we see a large difference in matriculation
18:692:67789:18:18:62:549:226:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:into medical school. Among applicants admitted in the first application cycle, 96% matriculated into a medical
18:693:67899:18:18:62:549:208:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:program. Among those who were not admitted in their first cycle (but could re-apply), the corresponding figure
18:694:68009:18:18:62:549:190:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:is 59%, giving us a large and precise first stage of 37 percentage point difference in the matriculation probability.
18:695:68126:18:18:77:549:172:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:The accepted and rejected students were equally likely to be women (57 percent in the accepted group) and
18:696:68231:18:18:62:549:154:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:had an equal number of siblings (1.82 in the accepted group). They had similar ages, although the accepted group
18:697:68343:18:18:62:549:136:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:is statistically (but not economically) significantly older (19.67 in the accepted group vs. 19.48 in the rejected
18:698:68457:18:15:62:549:118:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:group).38Accepted and rejected applicants were equally likely to be born in Sweden (97 percent in the accepted
18:699:68567:15:12:69:549:103:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:38The difference in age stems from the institutional nuances of the admission system – applicants can strengthen their applications
18:700:68698:12:10:62:549:91:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:by gaining five years of work experience; so, if there is a big time gap between the first and subsequent applications for some applicants
18:701:68836:10:9:62:549:81:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:who chose this route for their applications, we may in a small number of cases mis-classify the first application cycle and capture
18:702:68967:9:10:62:549:72:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:individuals who gained work experience before re-applying. The differences in age shrinks substantially when we zoom in into small
18:703:69097:10:0:62:549:62:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:subsamples, where we can more conservatively define the first application cycle and focus on high school graduates from the same
19:704:69227:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:group), and to have parents that were born in Sweden (87 percent of fathers and 86 percent of mothers born in
19:705:69336:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Sweden for the accepted group). Both groups had similar parental household income and father’s income, both
19:706:69443:18:18:62:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:measured before the applicant’s high school graduation and before the first medical school application cycle. A
19:707:69554:18:18:62:549:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:similar share of applicants had lost their father, or mother, or one of the grandparents by the year before the
19:708:69665:18:17:62:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:first application to medical school in the admitted and non-admitted groups (in the admitted group, 1 percent
19:709:69774:17:18:62:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of fathers, 1 percent of mothers, 57 (48) percent of paternal (maternal) grandfathers, and 32 (30) percent of
19:710:69883:18:18:62:429:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:paternal (maternal) grandmothers were deceased prior to the student’s application).
19:711:69966:18:18:77:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:In sum, 15 out of 16 observables are balanced across the admitted and non-admitted groups, and the t-test
19:712:70071:18:18:62:550:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:comparisons are far from any conventional significance levels with the lowest p-value of0.33(for whether the
19:713:70179:18:18:62:550:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:father was born in Sweden) for all observables except age. We conclude that the evidence in Table2 is consistent
19:714:70291:18:18:62:549:540:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:with an essentially random breaking of ties in medical school admission decisions for this group of highest GPA
19:715:70402:18:18:62:549:522:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:students. We thus proceed to use the first application cycle admission decision as an instrument for whether an
19:716:70513:18:18:62:252:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:individual matriculates into medical school.
19:717:70557:18:18:77:549:486:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:We report results (ITT and LATE estimates) separately for older and younger relatives of the health profes-
19:718:70664:18:32:62:395:468:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:sional, as the sets of relevant health outcomes and health investments differ.
19:719:70742:32:18:62:550:436:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f2:B:Health of older relativesTable3 reports our estimates of the effect of an individual gaining a medical
19:720:70844:18:18:62:549:418:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:education on the health outcomes of relatives aged 50 and above. For each relative, we track health outcomes
19:721:70952:18:18:62:549:400:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:starting in yeart+ 1after matriculation and untilt+ 8, which is the maximum time horizon that we observe in
19:722:71059:18:17:62:549:382:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:our sample. This time horizon captures the period of medical education, which typically lasts for 6 years, and
19:723:71169:17:18:62:284:365:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the first two years after medical school completion.
19:724:71221:18:18:77:549:347:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:For older relatives, we consider two sets of outcomes: (i) outcomes that capture preventive investments, and
19:725:71329:18:18:62:549:329:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:(ii) outcomes that capture physical health, in particular the life-style related conditions analyzed above. For
19:726:71440:18:18:62:549:311:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:preventive investments we focus on those that are likely to reduce the risk of life-style related conditions, and
19:727:71553:18:18:62:549:293:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:those that can be measured precisely in our data. In a final step, we aggregate all the specific outcomes into a
19:728:71665:18:18:62:466:275:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:single health index. All outcomes are scaled in per 1,000 individuals to aid in interpretation.
19:729:71760:18:18:77:549:257:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f2:A:Preventive investmentsWe consider eight measures of preventive investments that can be observed in our
19:730:71862:18:18:62:549:239:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:data: adherence to three types of drugs that reduce the risk of cardiovascular disease; adherence to diabetes
19:731:71971:18:18:62:549:221:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:drugs; take-up of Vitamin D (among women, for whom this vitamin is recommended in old age); adherence to
19:732:72075:18:18:62:549:203:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:asthma medication; the occurrence of preventable hospitalizations, and addiction to alcohol or drug substances.
19:733:72186:18:18:77:549:185:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Columns (1), (2), and (3) report the intent to treat (ITT) effects (with and without controls), and the local
19:734:72295:18:18:62:549:167:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:average treatment effect (LATE), respectively. In columns (4) and (5) we report two different benchmarks that
19:735:72404:18:18:62:549:149:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:are useful for interpreting the ITT and LATE coefficients. Column (4) reports a simple mean among family
19:736:72508:18:18:62:549:131:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:members of applicants who loose the lottery on their first application attempt. In column (5) we report the
19:737:72615:18:17:62:549:113:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:complier mean among control compliers. Within our control group, we observe individuals that decide not to
19:738:72721:17:18:62:549:96:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:attempt another medical school application when they loose the lottery. Conceptually, this group of individuals
19:739:72832:18:9:62:550:78:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:year – the sample of these individuals, however, is too small to perform our analysis. Hence, we keep the sample in Table2, and
19:740:72959:9:0:62:307:69:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:control for the year of birth non-parametrically in our regressions.
20:741:73029:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:includes (untreated) compliers and never takers. From2, we see that only 4% of individuals that win the lottery
20:742:73140:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:do not matriculate into a medical school, so the share of never-takers in our data is extremely low. In that
20:743:73248:18:18:62:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:case, family members of individuals who loose the lottery and do not re-apply, are predominantly compliers.
20:744:73355:18:18:62:549:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Computing the mean of outcomes among the family members of these individuals allows us to directly estimate
20:745:73462:18:17:62:522:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the mean of potential outcomes under no treatment for compliers. This is what we report in Column (5).
20:746:73564:17:18:77:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:We first study effects on adherence to chronic medication.  We measure adherence as the probability of
20:747:73666:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:purchasing medication conditional on having any condition that may warrant the need for this medication.39We
20:748:73774:18:18:62:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:consider three common cardiovascular drugs: statins (for lowering high cholesterol), blood thinners (for reducing
20:749:73887:18:18:62:549:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the chance of blood clots), and beta blockers (used for prevention and treatment in multiple cardiovascular
20:750:73994:18:18:62:549:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:conditions). Individuals in the treatment group, i.e., relatives of individuals who win the medical school lottery
20:751:74108:18:18:62:549:540:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:in their first application attempt, are substantially more likely to adhere to these medications. The effects are
20:752:74221:18:18:62:549:522:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:economically large for all three outcomes, and statistically precise for statins and blood thinners. For example,
20:753:74334:18:18:62:549:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:on average 247 out of 1,000 individuals in the control group purchase blood thinners, while in the treatment
20:754:74442:18:18:62:549:486:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:group it is 31 more people per 1,000 - a 13% increase (ITT). The effect of having a relative matriculate into
20:755:74551:18:18:62:549:468:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:medical school (on the compliers) is in turn larger, with 69 more people taking the blood thinning medication,
20:756:74661:18:18:62:549:450:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:which represents a 25% increase off of the control complier mean (LATE). The relative increases are qualitatively
20:757:74774:18:18:62:549:432:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:similar for the other two cardiovascular drugs: 27% and 9% increases in adherence to statins and beta blockers,
20:758:74885:18:18:62:549:414:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:respectively (LATE). Further, older family members of lottery winners are 20% (ITT) more likely to adhere to
20:759:74993:18:18:62:549:396:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:diabetes medication conditional on having the disease. Female older relatives also take prescription strength
20:760:75102:18:17:62:549:378:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:(rather than over-the-counter) vitamin D (vitamin D deficiency is common with aging, especially among women)
20:761:75210:17:18:62:549:361:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:at higher rates: 32 out of 1,000 women in the conditional complier mean take the vitamin, while 41 per 1,000
20:762:75318:18:18:62:549:343:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:more do among treatment compliers (LATE). We find positive but noisy differences in adherence to asthma
20:763:75421:18:18:62:549:325:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:medication. We find no systematic evidence of a decline in what we measure as preventable hospitalizations for
20:764:75531:18:18:62:549:307:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:older adults, but find some evidence of a decreased probability of addiction-related diagnoses in medical data,
20:765:75642:18:18:62:304:289:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:which captures addiction to alcohol or drug substances.
20:766:75697:18:18:77:549:271:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f2:A:Physical healthWe next turn to the analysis of the effect on physical health, in particular conditions that
20:767:75804:18:18:62:549:253:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:commonly are considered to be linked to lifestyle decisions. We find that 42 out of 1,000 individuals in the control
20:768:75920:18:18:62:549:235:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:group have a heart attack during our observation period. Among individuals whose relative wins the medical
20:769:76026:18:18:62:549:217:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:school lottery, the rate declines by 18 out of 1,000 people - a remarkable decrease of 44% (ITT). Exposure to
20:770:76135:18:18:62:549:199:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:a health professional among compliers leaves this group with only 14 per 1,000 individuals with a heart attack.
20:771:76246:18:18:62:549:181:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Importantly, as we are measuring the effects over a relatively short time frame, we cannot ascertain whether this
20:772:76359:18:18:62:549:163:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:decline is permanent or represents a short-run delay of this acute cardiovascular event.40We find similarly large
20:773:76472:18:14:62:549:145:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:effects on the probability of being diagnosed with heart failure: a decline of 27 per 1,000 individuals (ITT), or
20:774:76585:14:12:69:549:131:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:39In addition to the controls discussed above, the subset of regressions where the outcome captures individuals’ drug purchases
20:775:76712:12:10:62:549:119:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:also includes controls for the presence of asthma, type II diabetes, heart failure, ischemic heart diseases, stroke, hyperlipidemia, or
20:776:76847:10:9:62:76:109:8:g_d0_f6:6:g_d0_f5:F:hypertension.40
20:777:76862:9:10:77:549:100:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:In general, our estimates are not inconsistent with the results of related clinical trials; however, the direct comparison is hard
20:778:76992:10:9:62:549:90:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:to achieve for two key reasons: first, our timeline is actually long for the world of clinical trials, hence only few trials have been run
20:779:77130:9:10:62:549:81:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:over a comparable time period; second, nearly all large-scale clinical trials test the effect of one medication at a time, so that the
20:780:77264:10:9:62:549:71:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:composite effect of higher exposure to several cardiovascular medications at a time - which we are clearly observing in the data - is
20:781:77397:9:0:62:98:62:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:unknown.
21:782:77407:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:51 per 1,000 among compliers (LATE), off of the mean of 74 per 1,000 cases in the control group and 101 among
21:783:77516:18:18:62:484:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:control compliers. We do not find any evidence of a reduction of type II diabetes or lung cancer.
21:784:77613:18:18:77:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:To address the issue of inference with multiple outcomes and to improve statistical power, we aggregate all
21:785:77720:18:18:62:549:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:eleven measures into a “health index,” following the approach in Kling et al.(2007). We first orient all outcomes
21:786:77833:18:17:62:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:in the same qualitative direction (for example, for statins more is “good,” while for addiction less is “good”). We
21:787:77948:17:18:62:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:then construct a z-score for each outcome (subtracting the control group mean and dividing by the control group
21:788:78059:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:standard deviation) and take an unweighted average across all outcomes.41The result suggests that, among older
21:789:78169:18:18:62:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:adults, exposure to a family member who matriculates into medical school yields a large and statistically precise
21:790:78282:18:18:62:163:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:improvement in health.
21:791:78304:18:18:77:549:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:In the analysis of medical school lotteries, we are restricted to examining a shorter time horizon and have a
21:792:78413:18:18:62:549:540:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:limited sample, which likely accounts for the imprecise estimates for some conditions. At the same time, focusing
21:793:78526:18:18:62:549:522:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:on the shorter time horizon has the advantage of shedding light on the potential mechanisms at play in our
21:794:78632:18:18:62:549:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:findings. Since we mostly observe family members exposed to physicians in the family during their training and
21:795:78742:18:18:62:549:486:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:early on in their career, we can with high certainty exclude the possibility that the “access to care” channel is
21:796:78855:18:18:62:549:468:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:an important driver of these results. While in training, future physicians are exposed to a lot of information,
21:797:78966:18:18:62:549:450:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:but they cannot directly write drug prescriptions and are unlikely to have strong professional networks to enable
21:798:79079:18:18:62:549:432:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:them to help their family members “jump lines.” We return to the long-run analysis of the prevalence of chronic
21:799:79190:18:18:62:549:414:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:conditions and mortality in Section4.4, where we use a different empirical strategy to examine these important
21:800:79300:18:18:62:105:396:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:outcomes.
21:801:79309:18:17:77:549:378:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Overall, the point estimates in our analysis are consistent with the idea that older relatives of a physician are
21:802:79422:17:18:62:549:361:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:in better health and that they undertake more - cheap and simple - investments into their health, than similar
21:803:79532:18:32:62:539:343:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:individuals in families without a physician in training, and hence without informal access to health expertise.
21:804:79643:32:18:62:549:311:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f2:B:Health of younger relativesTable4 reports estimated effects of exposure to health expertise on the health

21:818:81126:10:9:62:76:110:8:g_d0_f6:6:g_d0_f5:F:faster.44

21:820:81261:10:9:62:549:91:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:themselves substituting away from hormonal birth control.  Concerns about the side effects of these medicines that have been
21:821:81385:9:10:62:549:82:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:documented in the clinical literature may drive this observation, although we cannot pin down the exact underlying mechanism with
21:822:81514:10:0:62:96:72:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:certainty.
22:823:81526:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:positive effect on take-up of the HPV vaccine. While 119 out of 1,000 individuals are vaccinated in the control
22:824:81637:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:group (174 among compliers), our estimates imply increases of 62 per 1,000 (ITT) and 202 per 1,000 (LATE) – an
22:825:81747:18:18:62:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:increase of more than 200% among compliers.45We estimate similarly large effects for the avoidance of hormonal
22:826:81857:18:18:62:549:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:contraception. While 655 out of 1,000 young women aged between 10 to 20 do not use hormonal contraception
22:827:81962:18:17:62:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:in the control group, 132 women (20% more) refrain from this form of contraception among those with a lottery
22:828:82071:17:18:62:372:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:winner (in the first application attempt) in the extended family (ITT).
22:829:82142:18:18:77:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:We further find large effects of being exposed to a health professional in the family on the probability of
22:830:82249:18:18:62:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:having an injury or poisoning that warrants a visit to a hospital (in inpatient or outpatient specialist care). The
22:831:82364:18:18:62:549:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:rate of substance addiction that warrants a visit to a hospital or specialist care among young individuals in the
22:832:82477:18:18:62:549:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:control group is 19 per 1,000; the corresponding number in the treatment group is significantly lower at 7 per
22:833:82587:18:18:62:198:540:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:1,000 - a decline of 63% (ITT).
22:834:82618:18:18:77:549:522:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Our estimates for inpatient stays paint a similar picture. We find that younger relatives of those who win
22:835:82724:18:18:62:549:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the lottery have a third of the number of inpatient stay days. We do not capture any differences in the rates
22:836:82833:18:18:62:549:486:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of severe injuries or poisoning (which are experienced by about a quarter of individuals in the sample), and we
22:837:82944:18:18:62:549:468:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:also do not find that being exposed to a health professional lowers the rates of respiratory infections, intestinal
22:838:83059:18:18:62:199:450:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:infections, or chronic tonsillitis.
22:839:83094:18:18:77:549:432:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Overall, we conclude that for younger generations, having a new doctor-in-training in the family appears
22:840:83198:18:18:62:549:414:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:to have positive effects on health: We see lower prevalence of addiction, fewer inpatient days, and a larger
22:841:83306:18:18:62:549:396:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:probability of preventive investments. Finally, we summarize our eight measures into a health index, constructed
22:842:83418:18:17:62:549:378:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:in the same way as for the older family members. The estimate suggests that, among younger family members,
22:843:83524:17:35:62:549:361:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:informal exposure to a health professional yields economically and statistically significant improvements in health.
22:844:83640:35:25:62:456:326:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:4.4  The event of a family member becoming a health professional
22:845:83704:25:18:62:549:301:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:While the Swedish medical school lotteries resemble an RCT and thus represent a near-ideal setting to examine
22:846:83813:18:18:62:549:283:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:causal effects, the short follow-up period precludes us from studying the long-run impact of exposure to expertise
22:847:83927:18:18:62:549:265:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:on older adults. We therefore complement this research design with event studies that exploit the timing of the
22:848:84038:18:17:62:549:247:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:arrival of a health professional in the family. Consistent with the analysis in Section4.3, we define the event
22:849:84149:17:18:62:549:230:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of a family member matriculating into medical school as the start of exposure to expertise.46Which families
22:850:84256:18:18:62:549:212:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:experience this event is not random. However, we can still assess whether having a doctor in the family impacts
22:851:84367:18:18:62:549:194:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the health of family members by observing how the trends in health evolve over time for families that experience
22:852:84479:18:18:62:386:176:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:this event relative to the trends in health in (similar) families that do not.
22:853:84557:18:18:77:549:158:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:In particular, we compare the families of individuals trained as medical doctors to the families of individuals
22:854:84668:18:18:62:549:140:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:trained as lawyers. Both types of families have similar socio-economic status, with income distributions that are
22:855:84781:18:18:62:549:122:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:skewed towards the top ventiles (although family members are present at all points in the income distribution).
22:856:84892:18:15:62:503:104:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Moreover, admittance into law school – a similarly prestigeous education – also requires a high GPA.
22:857:84992:15:12:69:549:89:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:45Interestingly, even in the families of compliers, we still only estimate an about 40% take up of this routinely recommended
22:858:85117:12:7:62:91:77:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:vaccine.
22:859:85125:7:0:69:540:70:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:A:46We do not require that the medical profession is pursued after college, though in practice the vast majority pursue medicine.
23:860:85254:0:18:77:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:We need two key identifying assumptions that appear plausible in our context. First, we require that access
23:861:85361:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:to health expertise arrives to families after an individual starts medical training. Second, for our results to be
23:862:85475:18:18:62:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:consistent with a causal interpretation, we need to assume that individuals do not decide to undertake medical
23:863:85585:18:18:62:549:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:training based on thetrendin the health of their extended family members. These assumptions appear plausible
23:864:85693:18:17:62:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:given the long timeline that typically accompanies the decision to pursue a medical degree and the slow process
23:865:85804:17:18:62:199:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of chronic disease development.
23:866:85835:18:18:77:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Before turning to a formal regression specification, we investigate whether the assumptions we require for
23:867:85941:18:18:62:550:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:identification, as well as the hypothesized effects, are supported by the raw data.  Figure8 documents raw
23:868:86047:18:18:62:549:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:differences in the probability of adverse health outcomes between individuals with a child who received a medical
23:869:86160:18:18:62:549:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:degree versus a law degree. In Panel8A, we plot mortality. In particular, we take the five cohorts of individuals
23:870:86273:18:18:62:549:540:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:born in Sweden between 1936 to 1940, and select individuals who have at least one child with a medical or law
23:871:86382:18:18:62:549:522:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:degree. We exclude individuals who are health professionals themselves (either a doctor or a nurse) or who have
23:872:86493:18:18:62:549:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:a health professional spouse.47In this sample, we compute the share of individuals that died by each calendar
23:873:86602:18:18:62:549:486:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:year starting with year 1980 (i.e. starting when the individuals are aged 40 to 45). We keep individuals in the
23:874:86713:18:18:62:550:468:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:sample even if they die, so the figure records cumulative mortality. Panel8B confirms that individuals in our two
23:875:86826:18:18:62:549:450:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:samples have identical average age. (This is what we would expect absent any dramatic–and unlikely–differences
23:876:86936:18:18:62:549:432:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:in the probability of having a lawyer or a doctor child across the 1936 to 1940 cohorts.) In earlier years, mortality
23:877:87053:18:18:62:549:414:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:rates are visually identical between the two groups. Around 1995 (ages 55 to 60), however, a diversion emerges
23:878:87163:18:18:62:549:396:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:between the mortality trends of lawyer-parents (hollow circles) and doctor-parents (filled triangles). Throughout
23:879:87276:18:17:62:549:378:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:years 1997 to 2017, parents of doctors are dying at a slower rate than parents of lawyers. The difference becomes
23:880:87389:17:18:62:549:361:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:economically and statistically significant over time, converging to a difference of 243 per 1,000 individuals having
23:881:87505:18:18:62:549:343:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:died among lawyers’ parents by 2017, as compared to 208 per 1,000 individuals among doctors’ parents. The
23:882:87610:18:18:62:450:325:10:g_d0_f2:7:g_d0_f4:B:difference of 35 per 1,000 lives (or 14%) is statistically significant at less than 1% level.48
23:883:87705:18:18:77:549:307:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:In Panels8C to 8F, we repeat a similar exercise for our set of four chronic, lifestyle-related conditions: heart
23:884:87817:18:18:62:549:289:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:attacks, heart failure, type II diabetes, and lung cancer. As our medical claims data starts much later than our
23:885:87929:18:18:62:549:271:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:mortality data, we track individuals starting in year 1997 (up until 2016). To be able to observe individuals
23:886:88038:18:18:62:549:253:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:prior to older age when the onset of conditions is already likely to have had started (and to increase precision),
23:887:88152:18:18:62:549:235:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:we increase the sample size by pooling the cohorts from 1936 to 1961. This cohort choice implies that we track
23:888:88262:18:18:62:549:217:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:individuals’ chronic diagnoses from the age of 36 to 81.  We observe remarkably similar patterns across all
23:889:88369:18:18:62:549:199:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of these conditions. As with mortality, in the early years of our data, the prevalence of chronic conditions is
23:890:88480:18:18:62:549:181:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:indistinguishable among individuals with a lawyer and a doctor child. Eventually, significant differences emerge,
23:891:88593:18:18:62:549:163:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:however, with parents of doctors having a persistently lower prevalence of all four chronic conditions. By the
23:892:88703:18:18:62:549:145:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:end of our sample period, in 2016, parents of doctors will have had 3 per 1,000 fewer heart attacks (7% fewer
23:893:88812:18:15:62:549:127:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:compared to the base of 42 heart attacks per 1,000 individuals in the lawyer-child sample); 4 per 1,000 fewer cases
23:894:88927:15:12:69:549:112:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:47For lawyer-parents we further exclude those who had a child that became a nurse, while for the physician-parents, we exclude
23:895:89053:12:7:62:365:100:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:those who had a child that became a nurse before another child became a doctor.
23:896:89132:7:12:69:549:93:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:48Note that in Sweden, it is extremely rare for individuals to reside with their children, even at a very old age; the social norm
23:897:89262:12:10:62:549:81:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:is that parents live alone and, if this is no longer possible, move into a long-term care facility (which is part of the municipal social
23:898:89399:10:0:62:355:71:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:insurance system). Thus, our results do not reflect an in-house caregiver effect.
24:899:89482:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of heart failure (10% fewer relative to the base of 40 per 1,000 among lawyer-parents); 8 per 1,000 fewer cases of
24:900:89596:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:type II diabetes (11% fewer relative to 76 per 1,000 among lawyer-parents), and finally 2 per 1,000 fewer cases
24:901:89707:18:18:62:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of lung cancer (18% fewer relative to the lawyer-parents baseline of 11 per 1,000 cases). All of these differences
24:902:89821:18:18:62:324:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:are again economically large and highly statistically precise.
24:903:89883:18:17:77:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:These sharp patterns in the raw data support our event study approach, as they suggest both that the
24:904:89983:17:18:62:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:deviation in the trend of chronic condition incidence and mortality happens long after individuals’ children
24:905:90091:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:are likely to decide to start their (undergraduate) degrees in law or medicine. Further, we observe non-trivial
24:906:90202:18:18:62:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:differences in the incidence of chronic conditions and mortality between these two groups of parents at older ages,
24:907:90317:18:18:62:464:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:despite their largely similar socio-economic standing (as illustrated in Appendix FigureA4).
24:908:90409:18:18:77:549:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:We now turn to a more formal analysis of these patterns and estimate the following event study-style speci-
