24:934:92338:18:18:62:549:188:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:degrees. Rather than excluding these individuals from the sample, we impute the timing of their degrees using
24:935:92447:18:18:62:194:170:10:g_d0_f2:7:g_d0_f4:B:high school completion year.49
24:936:92477:18:18:77:549:152:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Figure9 illustrates our results. We consider two main long-run outcomes: mortality and chronic conditions
24:937:92582:18:15:62:549:134:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:at older ages. For each health outcome, we plot the estimatedστ:s againstτ. Coefficient estimates for negative
24:938:92692:15:12:69:549:119:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:49For all individuals for whom we observe the year in which they acquire a medical (or law) degree, we count back 6 (or 5)
24:939:92814:12:9:62:549:107:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:years to define the matriculation year, as these are the common lengths of the undergraduate medical and legal programs. In event
24:940:92943:9:10:62:549:98:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:studies that examine mortality, we consider cohorts born in 1936 to 1940. In 17% of cases for doctor-relatives and 21% of cases for
24:941:93074:10:9:62:549:88:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:lawyer-relatives, we do not observe the exact year in which the relative acquired a medical or a legal degree. For these observations,
24:942:93208:9:10:62:549:79:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:we impute the age of matriculation as the year of high school graduation. In the analysis of chronic conditions, we observe the exact
24:943:93341:10:0:62:423:69:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:graduation date in 97% and 96% of cases, and impute the rest using high school graduation year.
25:944:93438:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f2:B:τ:s allow us to assess whether the data support the assumption that individuals are not sorting into the medical
25:945:93550:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:profession based on trends in familial health. Our estimates strongly support this assumption, which is consistent
25:946:93664:18:18:62:390:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:with our observations in the raw data on parental mortality and morbidity.
25:947:93738:18:18:77:549:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Panel (A) illustrates the impact of having a family member trained as a physician on the probability of
25:948:93841:18:17:62:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:death.50We observe a clear slow-down in the relative mortality rate among relatives of doctors (as compared
25:949:93948:17:18:62:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:to the relatives of lawyers) that starts emerging around year 8 after the young relative matriculates into college.
25:950:94063:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:The mortality gap then steadily widens for two decades. As Column (1) in Table 5reports, the point estimates
25:951:94171:18:18:62:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:suggest a 1.7 percentage point decrease in the probability of death by event time 25, which corresponds to a 10
25:952:94282:18:18:62:369:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:percent decline off the mean among relatives of lawyers, which is 17%.
25:953:94352:18:18:77:549:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Panel (B) of Figure9 captures the impact on the aggregated incidence of lifestyle-related chronic conditions.
25:954:94461:18:18:62:549:540:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:We plot the same “lifestyle” index that we examined in the non-parametric analysis, which is a z-score incorpo-
25:955:94572:18:18:62:549:522:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:rating the following conditions: heart attack, heart failure, type II diabetes, and lung cancer. Consistent with the
25:956:94688:18:18:62:549:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:observations in the raw data and our lottery-based results, we observe a significant divergence in health between
25:957:94801:18:18:62:549:486:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:relatives of doctors and lawyers that emerges around year 5 post college matriculation. The divergence widens
25:958:94910:18:18:62:482:468:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:for two decades post college matriculation, as can also be seen in Column 1, Panel B of Table5.
25:959:95005:18:18:77:549:450:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:We report separate event study results for the four chronic conditions underlying the lifestyle index in Ap-
25:960:95113:18:18:62:549:432:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:pendix TableA1, and graphically in Appendix FigureA5). We observe that differences emerge at around year 9
25:961:95219:18:18:62:549:414:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:post matriculation in the probability of having a heart attack and at around year 5 for congestive heart failure.
25:962:95332:18:18:62:549:396:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:The differences persist and expand over time. We observe a similar pronounced divergence in the incidence of
25:963:95440:18:17:62:549:378:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:type II diabetes and lung cancer. Fifteen years after matriculation, relatives of doctors are 1 percentage point
25:964:95552:17:18:62:549:361:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:(23 percent) less likely to have a diabetes diagnosis and 20 percent less likely to have lung cancer. These long-run
25:965:95668:18:18:62:549:343:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:patterns are consistent with the idea that responses to exposure to expertise include the formation of healthier
25:966:95780:18:18:62:549:325:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:behaviors and the adoption of new preventive measures, and that these long-run processes yield cumulative health
25:967:95892:18:18:62:235:307:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:benefits that grow important over time.
25:968:95931:18:18:77:549:289:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:As in the non-parametric analysis, we further examine the heterogeneity of our event study effects by income
25:969:96039:18:18:62:549:271:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:and proximity - both geographically and along the family tree. Columns (2) to (7) in TableA1 report the results.
25:970:96151:18:18:62:549:253:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:As in the non-parametric analysis, we find that individuals with income in the lower half of the distribution are
25:971:96264:18:18:62:549:235:10:g_d0_f2:7:g_d0_f4:B:more affected (we find 35% higher impact in the fist half of the income distribution) by exposure to expertise.51
25:972:96377:18:18:62:549:217:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Further, family members that live closer to each other geographically benefit more, which is consistent with
25:973:96485:18:18:62:549:199:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the importance of rich and persistent information transmission between the family member and the health
25:974:96588:18:18:62:549:181:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:professional, playing a key role in our results. We do not find substantial differences in the impact on mortality
25:975:96702:18:18:62:549:163:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:along the family tie dimension, while the impact on chronic conditions is stronger among closer family members.
25:976:96813:18:18:77:549:145:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Overall, we conclude that having a relative with a medical education has positive and quantitatively significant
25:977:96925:18:14:62:549:127:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:health benefits. These effects are present both at the top and at the bottom of the income distribution. In families
25:978:97041:14:13:69:550:113:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:50The outcome is an indicator taking the value of 1 if the individual has died by timet, and the value zero otherwise (i.e., if the
25:979:97172:13:9:62:76:100:8:g_d0_f6:6:g_d0_f5:F:individual is still alive in timet. The outcome thus captures the timing of death.51
25:980:97256:9:10:77:549:91:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:To facilitate the heterogeneity analysis by income and geography, we switch our sample to younger cohorts - 1946 to 1955. While
25:981:97383:10:9:62:549:81:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:our mortality records go far back, the information on income and geography is available for a more recent time period only. The
25:982:97510:9:0:62:451:72:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:difference in samples accounts for the differences in relative and point estimates across the specifications.
26:983:97621:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:with a physician, older relatives live longer and are less likely to experience common chronic conditions such as
26:984:97734:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:diabetes or a heart failure. Our event study results on long-run outcomes are qualitatively and quantitatively
26:985:97844:18:18:62:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:in line with our non-parametric and (short-run) lottery-based analyses, despite the fact that the three analysis
26:986:97956:18:42:62:294:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:samples are different and cover different time frames.
26:987:98010:42:30:62:396:623:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:C:5  Exposure to expertise and health inequality
26:988:98056:30:25:62:164:593:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:5.1  Mechanisms
26:989:98071:25:18:62:549:568:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:So far we have used three strategies to estimate the same empirical object - how the presence of a health
26:990:98176:18:18:62:549:550:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:professional in the family affects the health of family members. Having a health professional in the family is
26:991:98286:18:17:62:549:532:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:likely to affect individuals though multiple channels. We have focused our analysis on a set of outcomes that we
26:992:98398:17:18:62:549:515:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:argue are amenable to expertise, but that are unlikely to respond to other mechanisms. We lay this argument
26:993:98505:18:18:62:208:497:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:out in more detail in this section.
26:994:98540:18:18:77:549:479:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:There are two key other potential interpretations. First, our results could be driven driven by an income
26:995:98645:18:18:62:549:461:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:effect. Second, the effect of a health professional in the family could stem from access to care rather than access
26:996:98760:18:18:62:549:443:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:to expertise. This “social capital” channel would imply that health professionals get their family members more
26:997:98871:18:18:62:549:425:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:or betterhealthcarerather than to more or betterexpertise- for example, by getting them quicker appointments
26:998:98979:18:32:62:224:407:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:or advocating for costlier treatments.
26:999:99017:32:18:62:549:375:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f2:B:Income effectsIf there are economic returns to becoming a medical doctor (Ketel et al.,2016), so that
26:1000:99118:18:18:62:549:357:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:becoming a physician also affects the economic well-being of the household, then we might be concerned that our
26:1001:99229:18:18:62:381:339:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:estimates simply reflect the fact that families with a physician are richer.
26:1002:99305:18:18:77:549:321:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:There are several pieces of evidence that suggest that our results are unlikely to be driven by income effects.
26:1003:99416:18:18:77:549:303:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:In our OLS analysis, we flexibly control for individual income as well as for the income of the highest-earning
26:1004:99527:18:18:62:549:285:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:relative. In the event studies, to address the potential concern of income effects, we contrast family members of
26:1005:99640:18:17:62:420:267:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:physicians to family members of lawyers, who have similar overall income profiles.
26:1006:99722:17:18:77:549:250:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:There are several points to consider in the lottery analysis. First, we directly test whether there are income
26:1007:99832:18:18:62:549:232:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:gains to “winning” the medical school lottery over the time horizon we consider, and we find no such effect at
26:1008:99942:18:18:62:549:214:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:any conventional level of statistical significance. This is intuitive for two reasons. The time horizon we consider
26:1009:100057:18:18:62:549:196:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:encompasses primarily the years of training rather than the years of working as a physician. Further, for the
26:1010:100166:18:18:62:549:178:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:highest achieving students who apply to medical schools, the most common second-preferred option after medical
26:1011:100276:18:18:62:549:160:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:school is another high-income occupation, such as business or engineering (we can directly observe this in the
26:1012:100386:18:18:62:549:142:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:university applications data, which contains each applicant’s rank ordered list of university programs).52Second,
26:1013:100499:18:18:62:549:124:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:in the 2SLS specifications for the health outcomes of younger generations, we are effectively measuring effects
26:1014:100610:18:15:62:549:106:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:on the siblings and cousins of physicians, since only very few young doctors have children of their own over the
26:1015:100722:15:12:69:549:91:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:52This finding differs from Ketel et al.(2016) who do find financial returns to medical school in the Dutch setting. This likely
26:1016:100850:12:9:62:549:79:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:reflects differential distributions of salaries, differences in the details of the educational systems in the two countries, as well as
26:1017:100985:9:0:62:177:70:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:differences in the time horizon.
27:1018:101019:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:time horizon that we consider. The income of the physician is unlikely to have a direct effect on the physician’s
27:1019:101132:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:sibling’s or cousin’s household incomes. Finally, when we focus on older generations (in the 2SLS specifications as
27:1020:101247:18:18:62:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:well as in the event studies), then any economic returns to the profession of the child are indirect, since parents,
27:1021:101363:18:31:62:526:665:10:g_d0_f2:7:g_d0_f4:B:aunts/uncles, and grandparents are not likely to live in the physician’s household in the Swedish setting.53
27:1022:101471:31:18:62:549:634:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f2:B:Social capitalAnother mechanism through which the presence of health professionals in the family can affect
27:1023:101578:18:18:62:549:616:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:health outcomes is what we refer to as the access to care (or “social capital”) mechanism, where the impact runs
27:1024:101690:18:18:62:428:598:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:through preferential informal access to healthcare within the formally equal system.
27:1025:101774:18:18:77:549:580:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:It is instructive to distinguish between the access to expertise and access to care channels, which in principle
27:1026:101886:18:18:62:549:562:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:may exist in tandem, as they have distinct policy implications. Conceptually, responses that stem from improved
27:1027:101997:18:18:62:549:544:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:access to expertise may be scalable through policy interventions; we discuss this in more detail later in this
27:1028:102107:18:18:62:549:526:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:section.  Benefits that stem from improved access to formal care, in contrast, cannot be scaled with fixed
27:1029:102213:18:18:62:549:508:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:healthcare resources, almost by definition: If the family members of health professionals bypass other patients
27:1030:102324:18:18:62:549:490:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:who lack connections, then this implies a zero-sum game where connected patients benefit at the expense of
27:1031:102430:18:18:62:549:472:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:unconnected ones. Hence, it is important to understand whether there is any evidence suggesting the presence
27:1032:102538:18:18:62:549:454:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of the (potentially scalable) access to expertise channel. To do this, we focused our analysis in section4 on
27:1033:102647:18:18:62:506:436:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:outcomes that are more likely to be amenable to expertise and less likely to depend on access to care.
27:1034:102749:18:18:77:549:418:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Specifically, for older adults, we considered a set of chronic cardiovascular and metabolic conditions. The
27:1035:102856:18:18:62:549:400:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:prevalence and onset of these conditions is commonly attributed to lifestyle behaviors and adherence to medica-
27:1036:102967:18:17:62:549:382:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:tion rather than to any expensive (and hence potentially in shortage in the Swedish health care system) clinical
27:1037:103079:17:18:62:549:365:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:interventions. Further, improvements in these outcomes are not zero-sum: one patient avoiding a heart attack
27:1038:103187:18:18:62:549:347:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:does not come at the expense of another patient avoiding a heart attack, and so on. Second, we considered
27:1039:103292:18:18:62:549:329:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:preventive investments by older adults related to these lifestyle conditions: adherence to chronic cardiovascu-
27:1040:103403:18:18:62:549:311:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:lar medication, consumption of drugs for diabetes and asthma, and taking prescription strength Vitamin D.
27:1041:103508:18:18:62:549:293:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:A response in adherence to such drugs would very likely be driven by the expertise channel (which, broadly
27:1042:103614:18:18:62:549:275:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:defined, includes the provision of information about the benefits of these drugs; as well as reminders, nudges,
27:1043:103725:18:18:62:549:257:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:and “nagging” about drug adherence) rather than the access to care channel, as these medications are cheap and
27:1044:103835:18:18:62:549:239:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:easily obtainable – they are off patent, and included on the national prescription drug insurance formulary.54We
27:1045:103947:18:18:62:549:221:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:further investigated addiction andavoidanceof (potentially costly) hospitalizations, neither of which we would
27:1046:104057:18:18:62:217:203:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:expect to respond to access to care.
27:1047:104093:18:18:77:549:185:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Similarly, responses in the outcomes that we consider for the younger relatives are unlikely to stem from social
27:1048:104205:18:18:62:549:167:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:capital-type mechanisms. One patient obtaining the HPV vaccine or a non-hormonal method of contraception,
27:1049:104310:18:18:62:549:149:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:for example, does not come at the expense of another patient obtaining the same treatment. We also documented
27:1050:104419:18:18:62:549:131:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:a reduction in the number of inpatient stay days among family members of health care professionals; under the
27:1051:104528:18:14:62:549:113:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:access to care channel, we would have expected the reverse. Further, the rates of addiction and infections is likely
27:1052:104644:14:13:69:549:99:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:53The Swedish social insurance system stipulates widespread municipal care for the elderly that need long-term care, so even in
27:1053:104771:13:9:62:76:86:8:g_d0_f6:6:g_d0_f5:F:those cases any possible economic gains of the physician child are likely to be of secondary importance for health outcomes.54
27:1054:104897:9:9:77:549:77:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:In the lottery analysis, our results “show up” while physicians are still in training, and hence cannot prescribe these medications
27:1055:105028:9:0:62:267:68:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:themselves. This rules out “ease-of-prescribing”-effects.
28:1056:105087:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:to be diagnosed at higher rates conditional on the true prevalence of the disease among families with links to the
28:1057:105201:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:healthcare system; despite this, we consistently find either negative results or noisy zeros. In a nutshell, effects
28:1058:105317:18:18:62:371:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:on all these outcomes likely do not reflect the impact of access to care.
28:1059:105390:18:18:77:550:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:In sum, we establish impacts on outcomes that are inherentlynotzero-sum; that are driven by decisions that
28:1060:105496:18:17:62:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:individuals make in their everyday lives as opposed to actions by physicians within the healthcare system (lifestyle
28:1061:105612:17:18:62:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:decisions such as diet and exercise, tobacco use during pregnancy, and so on); and that involve adherence to
28:1062:105720:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:cheap and readily available drugs. These are outcomes for which “connections” to the healthcare system likely
28:1063:105829:18:18:62:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:matter very little. This is consistent with the fact that, in our lottery analysis, the “treated” group is exposed
28:1064:105943:18:18:62:549:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:to a young physician – either in medical school, or in the first two years after finishing medical training – who
28:1065:106056:18:18:62:177:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:likely has few connections.
28:1066:106083:18:18:77:549:540:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:In addition to focusing our analysis on outcomes that are likelynotdriven by access to care, we examine
28:1067:106186:18:18:62:549:522:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the importance of this channel directly. To do this, we investigate several outcomes that we can capture in the
28:1068:106297:18:18:62:549:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:data that reflect expensive or (in our setting) potentially rationed health care services, for which responses likely
28:1069:106414:18:18:62:331:486:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:would reflect the impact of connections rather than expertise.
28:1070:106476:18:18:77:549:468:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:First, we investigate whether family members of health professionals obtain more expensive heart attack
28:1071:106579:18:18:62:549:450:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:treatments.  The underlying idea is as follows.  There are two common invasive therapies, one of which is
28:1072:106684:18:18:62:549:432:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:substantially more expensive than the other, and one non-invasive (drug) therapy, which is the cheapest; under
28:1073:106794:18:18:62:549:414:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the “social capital” hypothesis, connected patients may be more likely to get a relatively expensive treatment
28:1074:106904:18:18:62:549:396:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:option (holding severity of the condition constant).55We find no evidence of differences in the probability of
28:1075:107014:18:17:62:549:378:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:getting an invasive (versus non-invasive) heart attack treatment across patients with and without an HP in the
28:1076:107124:17:18:62:549:361:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:extended family. Further, we find no difference in the intensity of invasive treatment conditional on getting an
28:1077:107236:18:18:62:285:343:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:invasive (i.e. surgery rather than drugs) treatment.
28:1078:107288:18:18:77:549:325:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Second, we investigate whether family members of health professionals have systematically longer stays in the
28:1079:107397:18:18:62:549:307:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:hospital after childbirth (conditioning on a wide range of characteristics capturing postpartum maternal health
28:1080:107508:18:18:62:549:289:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:and the child’s health at birth). Despite the fact that the duration of postpartum care is generally rationed in
28:1081:107620:18:18:62:549:271:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the Swedish healthcare system – mothers are discharged as early as six hours after childbirth, while mothers in
28:1082:107731:18:18:62:549:253:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the U.S. are legally entitled to stay for up to 48 hours, depending on the state – we do not find any differences
28:1083:107844:18:18:62:390:235:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:in the length of stay across patients with and without an HP in the family.
28:1084:107919:18:18:77:549:217:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Third, we examine the importance of the access to care channel for cancer treatment, as existing literature
28:1085:108026:18:18:62:549:199:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:has documented that connections appear relevant for the choice and speed of cancer treatments (Fiva et al.,
28:1086:108133:18:18:62:549:181:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:2014). Here, we do find a smaller time window between the first diagnosis of breast cancer and breast cancer
28:1087:108241:18:18:62:549:163:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:surgery among family members of health professionals. However, there is no pronounced income gradient in the
28:1088:108349:18:18:62:549:145:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:prevalence of cancers, nor in mortality attributable to cancer.56This suggests that, at the population level, the
28:1089:108462:18:14:62:549:127:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:access to care channel does not generate substantial differences in cancer-related outcomes across the income
28:1090:108571:14:13:69:549:113:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:55The two invasive therapies are coronary artery bypass grafting (CABG) and percutaneous coronary intervention (PCI), with the
28:1091:108697:13:9:62:76:100:8:g_d0_f6:6:g_d0_f5:F:former being a more expensive open heart surgery.56
28:1092:108748:9:10:77:549:91:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:In fact, if anything, we observe aninverseSES-gradient in cancers, which likely is driven by competing risks with cardiovascular
28:1093:108876:10:9:62:549:81:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:diseases as well as more screening at the upper end of the income distribution. The exception is lung cancer; however, it accounts
28:1094:109006:9:0:62:196:72:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:for a very small share of all cancers.
29:1095:109046:0:18:62:116:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:distribution.
29:1096:109059:18:18:77:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:To be clear, our investigation into access to care mechanisms is not exhaustive – this, however, is beyond the
29:1097:109169:18:18:62:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:scope of our paper. Overall, our focus on expertise-amenable outcomes allows us to argue that there exists an
29:1098:109278:18:18:62:550:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:effect of health professionals on their family members’ healththat does not run through social capital, and hence
29:1099:109391:18:17:62:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:that may be scalable. Moreover, our results point to simple interventions such as encouragement of vaccination,
29:1100:109502:17:18:62:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:promotion of adherence to basic chronic medication, and aid in cessation of tobacco use among pregnant women.
29:1101:109611:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:It is noteworthy that any interventions that increase these beneficial behaviors will have only a small effect
29:1102:109721:18:18:62:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:on health care expenditure. Moreover, they are cheap when compared to other potential interventions aimed
29:1103:109826:18:18:62:549:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:at improving population health, such as expansions of access to expensive treatments conditional on having a
29:1104:109934:18:35:62:95:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:disease.
29:1105:109942:35:24:62:349:523:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:5.2  Implications for the health-income gradient
29:1106:109990:24:18:62:549:499:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:So far we have showed that there is an average treatment effect of being exposed to a health professional in
29:1107:110098:18:18:62:549:481:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the family on health. We have also documented that the effects on health do not accrue only at the top of the
29:1108:110207:18:18:62:549:463:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:income distribution, but instead are similar, or even more pronounced, in the first half of the income distribution.
29:1109:110323:18:18:62:549:445:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:We now use these findings to create a “fully-informed” counterfactual. That is, we ask how the health-income
29:1110:110431:18:18:62:549:427:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:gradient would change if we made everyone in society exposed to expertise. We then discuss potential policy
29:1111:110538:18:18:62:549:409:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:interventions that could “mimic” intra-family expertise (without raising the number of health professionals in
29:1112:110648:18:18:62:274:391:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:families) for moving towards this counterfactual.
29:1113:110697:18:18:77:549:373:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:To create our counterfactual, we need two inputs: (i) the impact of expertise on health at different points
29:1114:110804:18:18:62:549:355:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:in the income distribution; and (ii) the baseline distribution of access to expertise in society today, i.e., in the
29:1115:110920:18:18:62:213:337:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:absence of any policy intervention.
29:1116:110955:18:18:77:549:319:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:It is straightforward to see why we need (i), and our finding that the beneficial effects of exposure to health-
29:1117:111067:18:18:62:549:301:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:related information are weakly larger at the lower end of the income distribution already suggests that a policy
29:1118:111179:18:18:62:549:283:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:that makes everyone exposed to expertise could close part of the health-SES gradient. If, in addition, individuals
29:1119:111293:18:18:62:549:265:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:at the lower end of the income distribution have access to less expertise, then this would further reinforce the
29:1120:111405:18:17:62:549:247:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:impact of policies that provide access to expertise on overall health inequality (as a larger share of individuals at
29:1121:111522:17:18:62:549:230:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the lower end of the income distribution would move from “unexposed” to “exposed” under such a counterfactual).
29:1122:111633:18:18:62:221:212:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Thus, we turn to a discussion of (ii).
29:1123:111671:18:18:77:549:194:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f2:A:The baseline distribution of expertiseIt seems a priori reasonable to hypothesize that individuals at
29:1124:111772:18:18:62:549:176:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the higher rungs of the income ladder have access to more expertise. Intuitively, they likely have had a longer
29:1125:111883:18:18:62:549:158:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:formal education, have access to more informed friends and relatives, a higher ability to search for information
29:1126:111995:18:18:62:549:140:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:on their own, and possibly more “mental bandwidth” to remember to take prescribed medications, among other
29:1127:112101:18:18:62:549:122:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:channels (Mullainathan and Shafir,2013). Table6 provides empirical evidence in support of this idea. Here,
29:1128:112207:18:18:62:549:104:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:we use data for Sweden from two waves of the European Social Survey, run in 2004 and 2014, when the health-
29:1129:112314:18:18:62:549:86:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:related questionnaires were included. We use six measures that may reflect the degree of access to health-related
29:1130:112427:18:0:62:549:68:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:expertise: (i) whether individuals agree to the statement that “a doctor always tells the truth;” (ii) whether
30:1131:112539:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:they prefer to see the same doctor over time; (iii) whether they regularly eat fruits; (iv) whether they regularly
30:1132:112653:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:eat vegetables; (v) whether they exercise regularly; and (vi) whether they smoke. The first two measures are in
30:1133:112764:18:18:62:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:principle indicative of the “demand” for expertise and trust-based relationships, which we would expect to be
30:1134:112873:18:18:62:549:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:higher if access to expertise outside of the formal healthcare environment is scarcer. The latter four measures
30:1135:112984:18:17:62:263:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:are indicative of individuals’ health behaviors.
30:1136:113032:17:18:77:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:We relate these survey responses to whether the individual has a college degree.  This is a measure of
30:1137:113134:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:socioeconomic status that is both available in the survey and allows us to connect the survey evidence to our
30:1138:113243:18:18:62:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:administrative data, since in the administrative data we observe the share of individuals with a college degree
30:1139:113354:18:18:62:549:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:at any point in the income distribution. As columns (1)-(6) of Table6 illustrate, we find a strong correlation
30:1140:113464:18:18:62:549:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:between formal education and our proxy measures for exposure to health expertise. This is consistent with the
30:1141:113573:18:18:62:544:540:10:g_d0_f2:7:g_d0_f4:B:idea that individuals with lower socioeconomic status have access to less health-related expertise at baseline.57
30:1142:113686:18:18:77:549:522:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Given this evidence, in our counterfactual calculation we use the share of individuals with a college degree as a
30:1143:113799:18:18:62:549:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:proxy measure for the prevalence of access to expertise. FigureA3 in the Appendix plots the share of individuals
30:1144:113911:18:18:62:549:486:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:with a college degree across the income distribution in Sweden. For the cohorts for which we consider mortality
30:1145:114022:18:18:62:549:468:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:outcomes by age 80 - 1936 to 1937 - 7% of individuals had a college degree in the lower half of the income
30:1146:114128:18:18:62:549:450:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:distribution, while 31% had a college degree in the top half of the income distribution.58The large difference
30:1147:114238:18:18:62:549:432:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:in formal education – and in the health-related survey responses associated with it in the ESS data – across
30:1148:114346:18:18:62:549:414:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the income distribution suggests that access to the type of expertise that is relevant for making decisions about
30:1149:114459:18:18:62:549:396:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:health behaviors and health investments likely is substantially scarcer at the lower end of the SES spectrum than
30:1150:114572:18:17:62:108:378:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:at the top.
30:1151:114583:17:18:77:549:361:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f2:A:A counterfactual: universal access to expertiseIn Figure10, we combine our findings into a back-of-
30:1152:114682:18:18:62:549:343:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the-envelope calculation of the potential effect of providing universal access to expertise on the mortality-income
30:1153:114797:18:18:62:549:325:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:gradient. We make the following two assumptions: First, we assume a uniform treatment effect of access to
30:1154:114902:18:18:62:549:307:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:expertise on mortality of 10% across the income distribution. This is our aggregate estimate from the event study
30:1155:115015:18:18:62:549:289:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:(which is consistent with the estimate from our non-parametric analysis); thus, it is a conservative estimate of
30:1156:115127:18:18:62:549:271:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the impact on mortality at the lower end of the income distribution. Second, we assume that the baseline level
30:1157:115237:18:18:62:549:253:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of expertise follows the same distribution as the college share, so that we start from a situation in which 7% of
30:1158:115350:18:18:62:549:235:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:individuals in the first half of the income distribution have access to expertise, while 31% do at the top. Under
30:1159:115463:18:18:62:549:217:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:these two assumptions, we compute the counterfactual mortality levels that would result, in the top and the
30:1160:115570:18:18:62:540:199:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:bottom halves of the income distribution, respectively, under a policy that gives universal access to expertise.
30:1161:115682:18:18:77:549:181:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:To compute counterfactual morality as the bottom (top) half of the income distribution, we start with
30:1162:115783:18:18:62:549:163:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:observed mortality by age 80 (at the level reported in Figure1A). We then assume that a hypothetical policy
30:1163:115890:18:18:62:549:145:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:moves the percentage of individuals that have access to expertise by 93 (69) percentage points (moving everyone
30:1164:116001:18:15:62:549:127:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:to 100%), and that these “treated” individuals experience a 10% reduction in mortality.59The calculation
30:1165:116105:15:12:69:549:112:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:57As a sanity check on the ESS survey data, we also verify that individuals without a college degree report being in worse health
30:1166:116234:12:7:62:165:100:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:in Column (7) of the Table.
30:1167:116261:7:12:69:549:93:6:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f6:F:58The gap in formal education is comparable for younger cohorts. In a pooled sample across all cohorts for whom we can observe
30:1168:116387:12:10:62:549:81:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:formal education levels, 16% of individuals have a college degree in the bottom half of the income distribution, and 44% in the top
30:1169:116518:10:9:62:76:71:8:g_d0_f6:6:g_d0_f5:F:half.59
30:1170:116525:9:0:77:549:62:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:The resulting formula for counterfactual mortality is: observed mortality within the income group times the treatment effect
31:1171:116651:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:suggests that a policy that creates universal access to health-related expertise by successfully mimicking intra-
31:1172:116764:18:18:62:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:family communication would shrink the mortality-income gap substantially: from the observed mortality gap of
31:1173:116872:18:18:62:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:0.076 between the top and the bottom halves of the income distribution, to 0.063. This corresponds to a 18%
31:1174:116979:18:18:62:239:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:reduction in the mortality-SES gradient.
31:1175:117019:18:17:77:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Our illustrative computation has important implications for health inequality, as it suggests that the asym-
31:1176:117127:17:18:62:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:metry in the quality and ease of access to health-related expertise across the socio-economic distribution can
31:1177:117237:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:generate and sustain a significant share of the health-SES gradient,evenin the presence of the equalized formal
31:1178:117348:18:18:62:296:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:access to healthcare, and a generous social safety net.
31:1179:117403:18:18:77:550:576:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f2:A:Towards closing the health inequality gapWhile the benchmark of universal expertise is instructive in
31:1180:117504:18:18:62:549:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:its own right – not the least by emphasizing that unequal access to expertise can, on its own, sustain substantial
31:1181:117618:18:18:62:549:540:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:health inequality – we now speculate as to whether our findings point to particular policy interventions that may
31:1182:117731:18:18:62:336:522:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:be able to scale up the beneficial impact of access to expertise.
31:1183:117796:18:18:77:549:504:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:One view of our results is that they emphasize the limits of government intervention.  Sweden provides
31:1184:117898:18:18:62:549:486:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:cheap and universal access to inpatient and specialized care, prenatal care, primary care, prescription drugs, and
31:1185:118012:18:18:62:549:468:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:vaccines; and yet substantial inequality remains. Our results indicate that this remaining inequality could in
31:1186:118122:18:18:62:549:450:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:part stem from decisions that individuals make outside of the healthcare system, such as whether to undertake
31:1187:118231:18:18:62:549:432:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:beneficial lifestyle investments, whether to adhere to prescribed (and cheap) drugs, whether to take up vaccines,
31:1188:118344:18:18:62:289:414:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:and whether to cease tobacco use during pregnancy.
31:1189:118394:18:18:77:549:396:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:On the other hand, our results suggest that a policy that were able to “mimic” what health professionals do
31:1190:118501:18:17:62:549:378:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:for their family members – and thus induce better drug adherence, a higher immunization rate, and cessation of
31:1191:118611:17:18:62:549:361:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:tobacco use in pregnancy, for example – would have the potential to make a substantial dent in population health
31:1192:118723:18:18:62:549:343:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:and reduce health inequality. It is thus worthwhile to consider the specific features of intra-family communication,
31:1193:118839:18:18:62:549:325:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:and whether a policy maker may be able to replicate (some of) those. If intra-family health professionals simply
31:1194:118951:18:18:62:549:307:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:transfer knowledge to their family members, then any information provision campaign may be effective.  To
31:1195:119056:18:18:62:549:289:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the extent that the power of intra-family communication about health stems from trust or detailed knowledge
31:1196:119163:18:18:62:549:271:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:about the health history and habits that come with a relationship that spans a long period of time, effective
31:1197:119272:18:18:62:549:253:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:policies may need to strive to mimic the depth of these relationships. We speculate that elements of such a
31:1198:119379:18:18:62:549:235:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f3:B:policy could include nurse outreach programs with a strong emphasis on the continuity of care (yieldinglong-
31:1199:119487:18:18:62:549:217:10:g_d0_f3:10:g_d0_f2:B:termrelationships), coupled with a strengthening of the role of a trusted and easily accessible - both in terms
31:1200:119598:18:18:62:549:199:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of geographic location and the administrative hurdles - general practitioner who knows patients, and potentially
31:1201:119710:18:18:62:550:181:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:their whole family, over a long period of time. Further,Alsan et al.(2018) suggests that providers which resemble
31:1202:119823:18:18:62:549:163:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the patient (in their case, same-race providers) may gain more trust. Finally, given the heterogeneous effects
31:1203:119933:18:18:62:549:145:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:across the income distribution, such programs specifically targeted at the poor may have the largest potential to
31:1204:120046:18:17:62:169:127:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:reduce health inequality.
31:1205:120071:17:10:62:549:110:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:(1-0.1), divided by (1-0.1*0.07) for the first half of the income distribution, and divided by (1-0.1*0.31) for the second half. The
31:1206:120203:10:9:62:549:100:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:denominator term re-scales the numerator to account for the differences in the baseline levels of access to expertise and hence the
31:1207:120334:9:0:62:201:91:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:share of individuals that gets treated.
32:1208:120375:0:28:62:163:719:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:C:6  Conclusion
32:1209:120388:28:18:62:549:691:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Growing evidence across various disciplines reveals stark correlations between health capital throughout the
32:1210:120496:18:17:62:549:673:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:course of life and a range of measures of socioeconomic status, such as education, social class, and income. Yet,
32:1211:120609:17:18:62:364:656:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the mechanisms underlying these associations are poorly understood.
32:1212:120676:18:18:77:549:638:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:A common explanation (and a policy focus) for the existence and persistence of health-SES gradients is the
32:1213:120782:18:18:62:549:620:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:difference in formal access to healthcare across the SES-spectrum. Our evidence suggests that this explanation can
32:1214:120896:18:18:62:549:602:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:only be one piece of the puzzle when it comes to understanding the origins of SES-gradients (as crucially distinct
32:1215:121010:18:18:62:549:584:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:from levels) in health. Using rich administrative data from Sweden, we document that strong socioeconomic
32:1216:121115:18:18:62:549:566:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:gradients in mortality and morbidity persist in Sweden, across a range of ages and conditions,despiteequalized
32:1217:121225:18:18:62:549:548:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:formal access to healthcare and a well-developed social safety net. This fact motivates us to examine a mechanism
32:1218:121338:18:18:62:549:530:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:other than access to formal health insurance and healthcare that may perpetuate socio-economic gradients in
32:1219:121445:18:18:62:92:512:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:health.
32:1220:121452:18:18:77:549:494:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Specifically, we investigate whether access to health-related expertise - throughout an individual’s lifetime -
32:1221:121563:18:18:62:549:476:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:can improve (the level) of health outcomes, while differences in access to such expertise at different points on the
32:1222:121679:18:18:62:344:458:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:socio-economic ladder can sustain inequality in health outcomes.
32:1223:121743:18:18:77:549:440:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:To create a quantifiable metric of access to expertise, we zoom into an environment where we can precisely
32:1224:121849:18:18:62:549:422:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:measure individuals’ exposure to health-related expertise: the presence of a health professional in the family.
32:1225:121960:18:17:62:549:404:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Using non-parametric evidence, event studies, and exploiting “admissions lotteries” into medical school, we find
32:1226:122072:17:18:62:549:387:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:that access to expertise has an important impact on health (level): children and adults that are “exposed” to a
32:1227:122183:18:18:62:549:369:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:health professional in the family live longer, are significantly healthier, are more likely to engage in preventive
32:1228:122298:18:18:62:549:351:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:health behaviors, and are more likely to adhere to medication. What’s more, the benefits of access to expertise
32:1229:122409:18:18:62:428:333:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:appear to be weakly larger for individuals at the bottom of the income distribution.
32:1230:122493:18:18:77:549:315:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:These estimates imply that the scarcity of access to expertise in households at the lower rungs of the socio-
32:1231:122602:18:18:62:549:297:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:economic ladder could create and sustain inequality in health outcomes — even in an environment with fully
32:1232:122708:18:18:62:549:279:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:equalized access to formal healthcare, generous social insurance programs, and a wide social safety net. It is
32:1233:122818:18:18:62:549:261:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:encouraging, however, that the benefits accruing to medical professionals’ family members appear to be scalable.
32:1234:122930:18:18:62:549:243:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Our analysis suggests that access to expertise improves health not through preferential treatment, but rather
32:1235:123039:18:18:62:549:225:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:through intra-family transmission of “low-tech” (and hence, cheap) determinants of health, likely ranging from
32:1236:123149:18:18:62:549:207:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:the sharing of nuanced knowledge about healthy behaviors, to reminders about adherence to chronic medication,
32:1237:123258:18:18:62:549:189:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:to frequent and trustful communication about existing health. This implies that public health policies, as well as
32:1238:123372:18:18:62:549:171:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:carefully designed public and private health insurance contracts that successfully mimic intra-famiy transmission
32:1239:123485:18:18:62:549:153:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of health-related expertise, would have the potential to close a significant share - our estimates suggest as much
32:1240:123599:18:0:62:214:135:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:as 18% - of the SES-mortality gap.

40:1447:139916:9:9:77:549:86:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:gradient for men at age 40 and at age 75 (p-values 0.46 and 0.87, respectively), as well as for women at age 75 (p-value 0.96).
40:1448:140043:9:10:77:550:77:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:F:We reject the equivalency for the mortality gradient for men at age 60 and for women at age 40 (p-values 0.00), and for women
40:1449:140168:10:0:77:274:67:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:A:at age 60 at the 10% significance level (p-value 0.05).

62:1991:174116:0:31:62:269:719:14:g_d0_f1:14:g_d0_f1:C:C  Further related literature
62:1992:174145:31:24:62:270:688:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:C.1  Early childhood interventions
62:1993:174179:24:18:62:549:664:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:A growing literature has documented that early life interventions have a positive effect on infant mortality and
62:1994:174291:18:18:62:549:646:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:can promote health in the long-run, suggesting that conditions in infancy are a relevant source of health and
62:1995:174400:18:18:62:549:628:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:socioeconomic disparities in later life. A Nurse–Family Partnership program in the US that provides regular
62:1996:174507:18:18:62:549:610:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:home visits by certified nurses to low-income mothers from early pregnancy until the child reaches the age of
62:1997:174616:18:18:62:549:592:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:two, has been found to have positive effects on birth outcomes and health in childhood (Agency for Healthcare
62:1998:174725:18:18:62:549:574:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Research and Quality,2014). For a universal home visiting program implemented in Denmark,Wüst(2012) show
62:1999:174829:18:18:62:549:556:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:that the intervention had a positive and significant effect on the infant first-year survival rate in Danish towns
62:2000:174943:18:17:62:549:538:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:and was most effective in the majority of small and medium-sized municipalities. The authors suggests that the
62:2001:175053:17:18:62:549:521:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:main driver of the programâs impact was the promotion of breastfeeding and appropriate infant nutrition by
62:2002:175159:18:18:62:549:503:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:visiting nurses. In a related study,Hjort et al.(2017) examine the long-term impact of the Danish home visiting
62:2003:175270:18:18:62:549:485:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:program.  They find that treated individuals that were visited by nurses in infancy experience better health
62:2004:175378:18:18:62:549:467:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:mid-life: they have lower mortality rates, spend fewer nights at hospital, and are less likely to be diagnosed with
62:2005:175493:18:18:62:549:449:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:cardiovascular diseases. Similarly,Butikofer et al.(2015) investigate the long-term impact of mother and child
62:2006:175603:18:18:62:549:431:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:health care centers in Norway and find that the increasing access to well-child visits had a positive effect on
62:2007:175714:18:18:62:549:413:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:health, education and earning of treated infants when they reach age 30 to 40. Moreover, the authors find a
62:2008:175821:18:18:62:549:395:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:stronger impact for children from lower socioeconomic background. Similarly, Sweden saw the introduction of a
62:2009:175930:18:18:62:550:377:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:nurse home visiting program in the early 1930âs andBhalotra et al.(2017) find that, in the long-run, the infant
62:2010:176041:18:35:62:481:359:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:care provided by nurse home visits reduced the probability of dying by age 75 by seven percent.
62:2011:176136:35:24:62:418:324:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:C.2  Community health workers and access to primary care
62:2012:176192:24:18:62:549:300:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Community health workers (CHWs) have been employed in many countries to provide health-related services
62:2013:176295:18:18:62:549:282:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:to their fellow community members.  Although there has not been many rigorous evaluations, most existing
62:2014:176399:18:18:62:549:264:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:evidence suggests that CHWs increase takeup rates of a wide variety of healthy behaviors and improve disease
62:2015:176507:18:18:62:549:246:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:management in the community, notably for health behaviors such as cancer screening and immunization, and
62:2016:176611:18:18:62:549:228:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:management of diseases such as asthma, hypertension, and diabetes (see e.g.,Norris et al.,2006;Haines et al.,
62:2017:176720:18:18:62:549:210:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:2007;Najafizada et al.,2015). In addition, by assisting individuals in navigating the health care system, CHWs
62:2018:176830:18:18:62:549:192:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:have been shown to improve access to medical services, especially for marginalized populations (Felix et al.,2011;
62:2019:176944:18:18:62:167:174:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Najafizada et al.,2015).
62:2020:176968:18:17:77:549:156:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Access to primary care in the community setting has also been found to be an effective way to improve
62:2021:177069:17:18:62:549:139:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:patients’ health.Bailey and Goodman-Bacon(2015) use the rollout of community health centers (CHCs) in the
62:2022:177174:18:18:62:549:121:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:U.S. from 1965 to 1974 to study the long-term health benefits of increased access to primary health care for the
62:2023:177286:18:18:62:549:103:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:poor. The paper finds that, in one decade after CHCs were established, CHCs reduced age-adjusted all-cause
62:2024:177392:18:18:62:549:85:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:mortality rates by 7 to 13 percent among the poor aged 50 and older, with the reduction primarily driven by the
62:2025:177503:18:0:62:549:67:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:decline in cardiovascular-related deaths. The authors argue that having access to a regular source of care, lower
63:2026:177618:0:18:62:549:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:medication cost, and improved compliance with prescription drugs were the main mechanisms for the effects of
63:2027:177726:18:18:62:147:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:CHCs on mortality.
63:2028:177744:18:18:77:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Moreover, a growing body of evidence suggests that the ease of access to nurses improves the health of patients
63:2029:177855:18:18:62:549:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:with chronic conditions.Fergenbaum et al.(2015) present a systematic review of six randomized control trials that
63:2030:177968:18:17:62:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:study the effects of home visits with nurse-led guidance in disease self-care management. Home visiting programs
63:2031:178080:17:18:62:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:result in fewer hospitalizations, fewer emergency department visits, and better patient quality of life. Studies
63:2032:178192:18:18:62:549:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:on nurse-led clinics that provide disease knowledge and support for disease self-care management report similar
63:2033:178303:18:18:62:549:594:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:health effects: these clinics significantly reduce patient emergency department visits, hospital readmissions, and
63:2034:178417:18:18:62:549:576:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:mortality rates, and improve patient medication adherence (Agvall et al.,2013;Gandhi et al.,2017;Liljeroos
63:2035:178523:18:35:62:160:558:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:and Strömberg,2019).
63:2036:178543:35:24:62:200:523:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:C:C.3  Patient education
63:2037:178565:24:18:62:549:499:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:An extensive body of work has evaluated the effectiveness of patient education interventions, finding such pro-
63:2038:178676:18:18:62:550:481:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:grams to be generally effective in promoting population health.  For chronic diseases,Stenberg et al.(2018)
63:2039:178783:18:18:62:549:463:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:review existing studies - 56 face-to-face intervention among patients living with chronic illess - on the impact
63:2040:178895:18:18:62:549:445:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:of education programs that target chronic obstructive pulmonary disease (COPD), asthma, chronic pain, heart
63:2041:179002:18:18:62:549:427:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:disease, and diabetes patients. The authors find that, regardless of study design and time horizon, interventions
63:2042:179115:18:18:62:549:409:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:that promote patient education are beneficial in terms of decreased hospital admissions, fewer visits to emergency
63:2043:179229:18:18:62:452:391:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:departments or general practitioners, and in terms of increased quality-adjusted life-years
63:2044:179320:18:18:77:549:373:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Similarly,Wang et al.(2017) review randomized control trials that investigate effects of self-management
63:2045:179424:18:18:62:549:355:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:education among patients with COPD. The paper highlights that such education programs improve patient
63:2046:179525:18:18:62:549:337:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:disease-specific knowledge and quality of life, and reduce respiratory-related hospital admissions and emergency
63:2047:179637:18:18:62:550:319:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:department visits.Anderson et al.(2017) focus on the educational component of cardiac rehabilitation for patients
63:2048:179750:18:18:62:549:301:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:with coronary heart diseases. The study reviews 22 randomized control trials that assigned patients to different
63:2049:179862:18:18:62:549:283:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:educational interventions that ranged from face-to-face counseling to residential stays with follow-up sessions.
63:2050:179974:18:18:62:549:265:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Patients in control groups received usual medical care in cardiac rehab that comprises exercise counseling and
63:2051:180084:18:17:62:549:247:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:training and psychological support. The paper finds that, although there is limited evidence that education-
63:2052:180192:17:18:62:549:230:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:based interventions reduce total mortality, the risk of a heart attack, or the number of hospitalizations, these
63:2053:180304:18:18:62:549:212:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:interventions result in lower risks of cardiovascular events and better quality of life. Similarly,Menichetti et al.
63:2054:180420:18:18:62:549:194:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:(2018) review randomized control trials that promote patient engagement among older adults with osteoporosis,
63:2055:180529:18:18:62:549:176:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:diabetes or cardiovascular-related health problems. The authors find that such interventions often demonstrate
63:2056:180639:18:18:62:338:158:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:positive effects on patient compliance with treatment regimens.
63:2057:180702:18:18:77:549:140:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:In the context of health behaviors,Aveyard et al.(2012) andStead et al.(2013) show that medical advice and
63:2058:180808:18:18:62:549:122:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:provision of behavioral or pharmaceutical assistance on smoking cessation increase the frequency and success of
63:2059:180919:18:18:62:549:104:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:smoking cessation attempts.Kaner et al.(2018) review the literature on alcohol interventions provided by health
63:2060:181030:18:18:62:549:86:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:professionals and conclude positive effects of these interventions on reducing excessive alcohol consumption. For
63:2061:181143:18:0:62:549:68:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:weight control,Aveyard et al.(2016) show that a randomized trial that provides interventions delivered by trained
64:2062:181258:0:18:62:383:719:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:general practitioners improves body weight control among obese patients.
64:2063:181330:18:18:77:549:701:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:A:Another strand of literature examines the effects of public health education campaigns promoted by social
64:2064:181435:18:18:62:549:683:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:media. A comprehensive summary of this literature can be found inGiustini et al.(2018). Many topics have
64:2065:181539:18:18:62:549:665:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:been included in these social-media education campaigns, including health behaviors such as smoking cessation,
64:2066:181649:18:17:62:549:647:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:healthy diet and physical activity (Chang et al.,2013;Williams et al.,2014;Swanton et al.,2015;Chakraborty
64:2067:181755:17:18:62:549:630:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:et al.,2018), and prevention and management of diseases such as diabetes and cancer (Gabarron et al.,2018;
64:2068:181861:18:42:62:538:612:10:g_d0_f2:10:g_d0_f2:B:Han et al.,2018). Existing studies generally suggest positive effects of these campaigns on population health.
